You: 

“We gaan werken aan een systeem om op een systematische, gestructureerde manier informatie, gegevens, data uit Wiktionary te halen. Weet je wat het verschil is tussen Wikipedia, Wikidata en Wiktionary?”

00:16

ChatGPT: 

Ja, ik kan je uitleggen wat het verschil is!

-   **Wikipedia** is een online encyclopedie waar je uitgebreide artikelen kunt vinden over bijna elk onderwerp. Het biedt gedetailleerde informatie en wordt geschreven door vrijwilligers.
    
-   **Wikidata** is een gezamenlijke database die gestructureerde data bevat. Het wordt gebruikt om informatie te bieden aan verschillende projecten, zoals Wikipedia en andere websites. Wikidata slaat gegevens op in een gestandaardiseerd formaat, wat het makkelijk maakt om data te delen en te hergebruiken.
    
-   **Wiktionary** is een online woordenboek dat definities, vertalingen, uitspraak, en etymologie van woorden biedt in verschillende talen.
    

Dus, Wikipedia is voor uitgebreide artikelen, Wikidata is voor gestructureerde data, en Wiktionary is een woordenboek.

You: 

“Oké, Wikipedia bestaat in verschillende talen, dat betekent dat voor de talen waarvoor er informatie is een bepaald concept op de Engelse Wikipedia kan bestaan, op de Nederlandstalige, Duitse, Spaanse, enzovoort, Russisch, en wat er ook maar allemaal is. Die artikelen die over hetzelfde concept gaan op Wikipedia hebben een Unique Wikidata ID, een Global Unique Identification. Dat ID zorgt ervoor dat een concept dat op de Engelse Wikipedia pagina gekoppeld kan worden aan informatie die staat op de Nederlandse Wikipedia, Duitse, Franse, Russische, enzovoort. Mijn vraag is of Wiktionary ook deelneemt aan Wikidata voor het gebruik van unieke identifiers.”

00:56

ChatGPT: 

Wiktionary maakt ook gebruik van Wikidata, maar op een iets andere manier dan Wikipedia. Wiktionary-artikelen bevatten vaak links naar gerelateerde Wikidata-items, vooral voor informatie over etymologie, vertalingen en taalkundige details. Wiktionary gebruikt echter niet altijd unieke Wikidata-ID's voor elk woord zoals Wikipedia dat doet. In plaats daarvan worden Wiktionary-artikelen vaak gelinkt aan Wikidata-items die relevante taal- en definitiegerelateerde gegevens bevatten.

Dus hoewel Wiktionary en Wikipedia beide gebruik maken van Wikidata voor gestructureerde data, is de mate van integratie en het gebruik van unieke ID's iets anders.

You: 

“Oké, voor Wikipedia, Wikidata en Wiktionary bestaan er APIs. Ik heb een beetje ervaring met de API van Wikipedia, maar van Wiktionary ben ik een beetje in het duister. Kan je mij zeggen wat voor informatie de API van Wiktionary kan aanbieden op een gestructureerde manier?”

00:26

ChatGPT: 

De API van Wiktionary is minder gestandaardiseerd en minder uitgebreid dan die van Wikipedia of Wikidata. Wiktionary is vooral gericht op taalkundige informatie en definities. De API van Wiktionary biedt toegang tot een aantal soorten gegevens, zoals:

1.  **Woorden en Definities**: De API kan details geven over woorden, zoals definities, vertalingen, synoniemen, en voorbeeldzinnen.
    
2.  **Etymologie**: Informatie over de oorsprong van een woord en de historische ontwikkeling ervan.
    
3.  **Vertalingen**: Woordenboekvertalingen van een bepaald woord in andere talen.
    
4.  **Uitspraak**: Informatie over hoe een woord wordt uitgesproken, inclusief fonetische transcripties.
    

De API van Wiktionary is echter minder gestandaardiseerd en gedocumenteerd dan die van Wikipedia of Wikidata. Dit betekent dat je mogelijk wat extra werk moet doen om de gewenste gegevens op te halen en te verwerken. Het is een handige bron voor taalkundige en lexicale gegevens!

```
voorbeelden:  
  - zin: "Al wat gij ooit hebt gewild, het werd u gegeven."  
  - zin: "Jullie wisten niet wat jullie werten."  
synoniemen:  
  - "werd"  
  - "werden"  
gebruik:  
  - context: "Gebruikelijk in oudere teksten, poëzie, of literaire stijlen."  
  - opmerking: "Heden de dag wordt het zelden gebruikt in de gesproken taal."
```

Dit bestand bevat meer gedetailleerde en concrete informatie, zoals de betekenis, etymologie, voorbeeldzinnen, en synoniemen, zodat het vollediger aansluit bij de gegevens die je op de Wiktionary-pagina kunt vinden. Wat denk je van deze versie?

# 📦 Mogelijke gestructureerde output (conceptueel model)

Hieronder geef ik je een **realistisch YAML-model** dat overeenkomt met wat je effectief uit Wiktionary kunt halen.

```
YAML

query:  
  input: "έγραψε"  
  language: "el"  
  normalized: "έγραψε"  
  has\_accent: true  
  
entry:  
  type: "inflected\_form"  
  part\_of\_speech: "verb"  
  
  inflection:  
    lemma: "γράφω"  
    tense: "aorist"  
    voice: "active"  
    mood: "indicative"  
    person: 3  
    number: "singular"  
    augment: "έ-"  
    stem: "γραψ-"  
    ending: "-ε"  
  
  morphology:  
    verb\_class: "omega\_verb"  
    aorist\_type: "sigmatic"  
    stem\_allomorphy:  
      present: "γραφ-"  
      aorist: "γραψ-"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ˈeɣrapse/"  
    hyphenation: "έ-γρα-ψε"  
  
  etymology:  
    from\_ancient\_greek: "ἔγραψε"  
    root: "γράφω"  
    PIE\_root: "\*gerbh- (to scratch, carve)"  
  
  related\_forms:  
    present\_1sg: "γράφω"  
    imperfect\_3sg: "έγραφε"  
    aorist\_1sg: "έγραψα"  
    participle: "γραμμένος"  
    passive\_aorist: "γράφτηκε"  
  
  lexical\_relations:  
    derived\_terms:  
      - "γραφή"  
      - "γράμμα"  
      - "γραφικός"  
      - "συγγραφέας"  
    compounds:  
      - "υπογράφω"  
      - "περιγράφω"  
  
  usage:  
    example:  
      - "Έγραψε ένα γράμμα."  
        translation: "He/she wrote a letter."
```

---

# 🎯 Wat is hier belangrijk voor jouw systeem?

## 1️⃣ Vorm → lemma mapping

Wiktionary vermeldt expliciet:

> "τρίτο ενικό πρόσωπο οριστικής αορίστου του ρήματος γράφω"

Dat is precies wat jij nodig hebt:

```
Code

inflected\_form → lemma
```

Dit is de kritische stap in jouw pipeline.

---

## 2️⃣ Morfologische granulariteit

Je kan structureel extraheren:

-   tense
    
-   voice
    
-   mood
    
-   person
    
-   number
    
-   augment
    
-   stamwissel (γραφ → γραψ)
    

Voor jouw Griekse inflectionele families is dit extreem waardevol.

---

## 3️⃣ Wat krijg je NIET rechtstreeks via API?

Belangrijk:

Wiktionary heeft geen mooie, nette morfologische JSON-API zoals Wikidata.

Je krijgt:

-   Wikitext
    
-   of HTML
    

Dus je moet:

-   templates parsen (zoals {{el-verb-form}})
    
-   of MediaWiki API gebruiken en wikitext structureren
    

---

# 🧠 Architectuuradvies voor jouw TypeScript package

Pipeline:

```
Code

input string  
   ↓  
query Wiktionary page  
   ↓  
detect "verb form of"  
   ↓  
extract lemma  
   ↓  
fetch lemma page  
   ↓  
extract full conjugation table  
   ↓  
normalize into internal morphological schema
```

---

# ⚠️ Belangrijke technische realiteit

Voor Grieks is Wiktionary veel consistenter dan voor veel andere talen, omdat:

-   vaste templates gebruikt worden
    
-   conjugatietabellen via sjablonen gegenereerd worden
    
-   morfologische labels relatief systematisch zijn
    

Dat maakt scraping veel betrouwbaarder.

---

# 🚀 Wat kan je theoretisch terugkrijgen?

Samengevat kan jouw systeem volgende datacategorieën genereren:

| Categorie | Beschikbaar |
| --- | --- |
| lemma | ✅ |
| volledige morfologie | ✅ |
| conjugatietabel | ✅ |
| IPA | ✅ |
| etymologie | ✅ |
| afleidingen | ✅ |
| samenstellingen | ✅ |
| voorbeeldzinnen | soms |
| frequentie | ❌ |
| CEFR | ❌ |

Frequentie en CEFR moet je elders halen (bv. corpora).

-   een formeel TypeScript interface-schema ontwerpen
    
-   of een robuust Wiktionary extraction model specificeren
    
-   of een generiek YAML v2 morfologisch model ontwerpen dat voor meerdere talen werkt
    

Wat wil je als volgende stap?

You: 

geef me de link/URL/query voor de Wiktionary REST API, met zoekterm "έγραψε".

ChatGPT: 

Hier is hoe je **de Wiktionary-REST-API** kunt gebruiken om informatie over *έγραψε* op te halen — inclusief de exacte URL en query-voorbeeld die je kunt gebruiken vanuit een script, zoals in TypeScript.

---

## 📌 Officiële Wikimedia REST API (voor Wiktionary)

Wiktionary ondersteunt **dezelfde REST-API-endpoints als andere Wikimedia-projecten**, waaronder:

```
Code

https://<wiki-domain>/api/rest\_v1/page/...
```

Waarbij:

-   `<wiki-domain>` → de hoofd-URL van de specifieke Wiktionary-versie (bijv. **el.wiktionary.org**, **nl.wiktionary.org**, **en.wiktionary.org**) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Wikimedia_REST_API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    

---

## 🔍 REST API endpoint — *page/html*

Om de **HTML-weergave van de pagina** voor *έγραψε* op te halen via REST:

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/html/έγραψε
```

Of, voor de Engelse Wiktionary:

```
Code

https://en.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/html/έγραψε
```

Deze URL levert **geparseerde HTML** terug waar je vervolgens structuur uit kunt halen.

---

## 📄 REST API endpoint — *page/mobile-text*

Een andere nuttige REST-endpoint (voor meer platte tekst):

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/mobile-text/έγραψε
```

Of:

```
Code

https://en.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/mobile-text/έγραψε
```

Dit geeft je redelijk schone tekst met secties zoals “Μορφή”, “Προφορά”, “Ετυμολογία”, enz. — wat makkelijker is om te parseren dan hele HTML-pagina’s.

---

## 📊 REST API endpoint — *page/summary*

Een kort samenvattend resultaat:

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/summary/έγραψε
```

Of:

```
Code

https://en.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/summary/έγραψε
```

De summary geeft:

-   Page-title
    
-   Extract (korte samenvatting)
    
-   Language
    
-   Pagina-URL
    

Deze gegevens zijn **JSON-gestructureerd** en handig voor snelle zoekresultaten.

---

## 🔗 Voorbeeldqueries

### 1) HTML-weergave (volle pagina via REST)

```
http

GET https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/html/έγραψε
```

→ HTML, geschikt voor downstream parsing.

---

### 2) Samenvatting (JSON)

```
http

GET https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/summary/έγραψε
```

→ JSON met summary/inleiding.

---

### 3) Mobiele tekst (platttere content)

```
http

GET https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest\_v1/page/mobile-text/έγραψε
```

→ Text zonder full HTML.

---

## 🧠 Belangrijke notitie

Wiktionary zelf heeft **geen aparte “dictionary/definitions” REST-API zoals Wikipedia** (bijv. `/definition/<term>`). Het REST-API-aanbod volgt de **MediaWiki REST API structuur**, welke vooral pagina-content en metadata biedt — niet gestructureerde lexicale data zoals definities met labels voor grammatica. [en.wiktionary.org+1](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/User%3AAmgine/Wiktionary_data_%26_API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

Dus:

✔️ Je kunt de Wiktionary-pagina ophalen via REST  
❌ Je krijgt daar niet automatisch een kant-en-klare JSON-lexicale structuur

→ Je toepassing moet de HTML of mobile-text parseren om:

-   lemma identificatie
    
-   morfologische labels
    
-   definities
    
-   voorbeeldzinnen
    

uit de Wiktionary-tekst te extraheren.

---

## 📌 Samengevat: basis REST API links

| Doel | URL (example) |
| --- | --- |
| HTML content | `https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest_v1/page/html/έγραψε` |
| Mobile text | `https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest_v1/page/mobile-text/έγραψε` |
| JSON summary | `https://el.wiktionary.org/api/rest_v1/page/summary/έγραψε` |

(Vervang `el.wiktionary.org` door een andere Wiktionary-uitgave als gewenst.) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Wikimedia_REST_API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

Wil je dat ik je een klein TypeScript-voorbeeld geef om deze REST-API aan te roepen en de respons te parsen? (Bijv. met `fetch` of met een parser die HTML → JSON omzet.)

You: 

Ik denk dat het goed is dat we vanuit Dictionary eigenlijk geen JSON response kunnen terugkrijgen en dat we dus altijd HTML moeten parsen met de woorden scrapen.

ChatGPT: 

Enkele seconden nagedacht

Je intuïtie klopt **gedeeltelijk**, maar ik zou het net iets scherper formuleren:

-   **Wiktionary biedt géén “dictionary-JSON”** (geen nette, semantische API die je meteen *definities/pos/inflectie/etymologie* als afzonderlijke velden teruggeeft). [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/User%3AAmgine/Wiktionary_data_%26_API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
-   Maar dat betekent niet dat je **altijd HTML moet scrapen**. Je hebt grofweg **drie** praktische opties:
    

## 1) Wikitext ophalen (Action API) en zelf templates parsen

Je kunt de ruwe wikicode krijgen via `action=query&prop=revisions` (of modernere varianten) en dan de sjablonen zoals `{{...}}` deterministisch ontleden. [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3ARevisions?utm_source=chatgpt.com)  
Voordeel: stabieler dan HTML, en je ziet exact welke templates gebruikt worden.  
Nadeel: je moet een goede wikitext/template parser bouwen (maar dat is precies jouw “systematische extractor”-ambitie).

## 2) Server-side parsing door MediaWiki (Action API `action=parse`)

Je kunt MediaWiki zelf laten parsen en dan HTML (of andere parser-output) terugkrijgen. [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)  
Voordeel: minder werk dan volledige wikitext parsing.  
Nadeel: je krijgt nog steeds geen “dictionary JSON”; je krijgt *presentatie-HTML* die kan veranderen.

## 3) REST `page/html` (Parsoid) en DOM parsing

Het REST endpoint `.../api/rest_v1/page/html/<title>` is in feite Parsoid-HTML. Parsoid is expliciet bedoeld om wikitext ↔ HTML te converteren (met extra metadata voor round-tripping). [MediaWiki+2MediaWiki+2](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Parsoid/API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)  
Voordeel: consistenter DOM dan “random HTML-scrape”.  
Nadeel: nog altijd geen semantisch JSON; je moet DOM/secties interpreteren.

---

# Mijn advies voor jouw package (TS/Node)

Voor een robuuste, taal-agnostische extractor:

**Primary source = wikitext**, want daar zit de “waarheid” (templates, labels, parameters).  
**Secondary = Parsoid HTML** als fallback/extra, vooral voor presentatielaag en snelle prototyping.

Praktisch betekent dat: je bouwt een pipeline die eerst probeert:

1.  lemma/inflected-form relatie uit de templates te halen (wikitext)
    
2.  en pas als dat faalt: Parsoid HTML inspecteren

ChatGPT: 

Niet per se “een hele zieke tech-parser” — maar je hebt wél gelijk dat **Wiktionary geen kant-en-klare lexicale JSON-API** is. De truc is: **je bouwt geen algemene wikitext-parser**, je bouwt een **template/sectie-extractor met beperkte scope**.

Concreet: je hoeft maar een klein aantal *structurele ankers* te ondersteunen om jouw use case (vorm → lemma → inflectie + kernmetadata) betrouwbaar te maken.

## Een realistische, niet-gekke aanpak

### 1) Ga niet voor “parse alles”, ga voor “extract de invarianten”

Voor jouw doel heb je vooral nodig:

-   **Form-of relatie**: “έγραψε is aorist 3sg of γράφω”
    
-   **Lemma-pagina kernvelden**: POS, definities, IPA, etymologie (optioneel), inflectietabel (optioneel)
    

Dat kan je vaak halen uit:

-   **sectiekoppen** (`==Greek==`, `===Verb===` etc.)
    
-   **templates** (vooral “form-of” templates)
    
-   **bullets/definition lines** (`# ...`)
    

Je negeert 80% van de rest.

### 2) Kies één “bronformaat” en maak een fallback

-   **Primair**: wikitext via MediaWiki Action API (stabieler dan HTML)
    
-   **Fallback**: REST `page/html` (Parsoid) als jouw wikitext-extractor faalt
    

Zo vermijd je fragile “scraping”.

### 3) Bouw het als een set kleine recognizers, niet als een compiler

Denk in plug-ins:

-   `detectLanguageSections(wikitext)`
    
-   `extractPOSBlocks(section)`
    
-   `extractFormOf(templateCalls)`
    
-   `extractIPA(pronunciationBlock)`
    
-   `extractDefinitions(defLines)`
    

Elke stap is klein en testbaar.

## Waarom dit minder erg is dan het klinkt

-   Wiktionary gebruikt **heel herhaaldelijke templates**.
    
-   Voor jouw scenario (Grieks/Modern Greek) zijn de “form-of” pagina’s meestal **vrij consistent**.
    
-   Je kan starten met **10 templates** en later uitbreiden.
    

## Minimal viable scope (wat je *echt* moet kunnen)

Voor “έγραψε” wil je MVP:

1.  **Bestaat de pagina?**
    
2.  **Welke taal-sectie?** (Greek / Modern Greek)
    
3.  **Welke POS?** (verb form / verb)
    
4.  **Form-of template vinden** → lemma = γράφω + features
    
5.  (optioneel) lemma-pagina fetch → definities + IPA
    

Dat is haalbaar zonder “mega parser”.

## Extra pragmatische ontsnappingsroute (als je sneller wil)

Er bestaan community datasets die Wiktionary al “gestructureerd” hebben (bv. via periodic dumps → JSON). Dan hoef je niet live te parsen, maar werk je op een lokale index. Dat is vaak sneller én stabieler, maar vraagt data-pipeline/hosting.

You’re right to challenge that — **those `.../api/rest_v1/page/summary/...` URLs are not reliable on el.wiktionary**, and in your case they clearly **don’t work**.

What I gave you there was the **old “Wikimedia RESTBase” style** (`/api/rest_v1/...`), which is still used on some Wikimedia projects (famously Wikipedia), but **not necessarily enabled/available on every Wiktionary domain**. On **el.wiktionary** it appears to be **absent / blocked**, hence the errors you saw.

## Use these endpoints instead (they’re the current, documented MediaWiki REST API)

MediaWiki’s current REST API lives under:

> `https://<domain>/w/rest.php/v1/...` [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API/Reference)

So for your term **έγραψε**:

### 1) Get page “source” + metadata (JSON)

This returns a “page object” including the **source** (wikitext) and revision/license metadata:

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/w/rest.php/v1/page/%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5
```

(That route is documented as `GET /page/{title}`.) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API/Reference)

### 2) Get page content as HTML

If you explicitly want HTML:

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/w/rest.php/v1/page/%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5/html
```

(That route is documented as “Get the content … in HTML”.) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API/Reference)

### 3) Get page metadata + HTML in one JSON payload

This variant is often convenient:

```
Code

https://el.wiktionary.org/w/rest.php/v1/page/%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5/with\_html
```

(See the docs examples using `/with_html`.) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API/Reference)

---

## If you prefer the classic Action API (very useful for wikitext)

You can also reliably fetch wikitext via the Action API and/or ask MediaWiki to parse it: [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

Example (parse an existing page, get structured parse output):

```
Plain text

https://el.wiktionary.org/w/api.php?action=parse&page=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5&prop=wikitext|sections|templates&format=json
```

Docs for parsing wikitext (`action=parse`): [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)  
Docs for getting page contents via revisions: [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AGet_the_contents_of_a_page?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## Why you got “Domain not allowed”

Given your report, that message is consistent with **hitting an endpoint that is not enabled/allowlisted on that domain** (RESTBase-style routes on that wiki), rather than anything to do with your query string.

So: **your conclusion is correct** — don’t build on `/api/rest_v1/page/summary` for Wiktionary. Build on:

-   **MediaWiki REST API**: `/w/rest.php/v1/page/...` (JSON/HTML) [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API/Reference)
    
-   **Action API**: `/w/api.php` for wikitext + parsing [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

# 🔴 Critical Design Insight

Wiktionary is **not language-partitioned lexically**.

Unlike Wikipedia (where each language has its own encyclopedia),  
Wiktionary language editions are editorial communities — not lexical partitions.

-   `en.wiktionary.org` → contains entries for Greek, Dutch, Japanese, etc.
    
-   `el.wiktionary.org` → contains entries too, but coverage differs.
    
-   They are not mirrors of each other.
    

So:

**The correct API domain depends on where the entry actually exists.**

---

# ✅ What you should do instead

For lexicographic extraction, you should:

## Always query **en.wiktionary.org**

Because:

-   It has the most complete coverage
    
-   It standardizes language sections inside the page
    
-   It is structurally more consistent
    
-   It is the de facto canonical Wiktionary for data extraction
    

So this works:

```
Code

https://en.wiktionary.org/w/rest.php/v1/page/%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5
```

And this works with the Action API:

```
Code

https://en.wiktionary.org/w/api.php?action=parse&page=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5&format=json&prop=wikitext
```

---

# 🟢 So are we forced to scrape HTML?

No.

You are forced to:

-   Use **the correct domain**
    
-   Accept that Wiktionary has **no lexical JSON API**
    
-   Extract structure from either:
    
    -   Wikitext (recommended)
        
    -   Parsoid HTML (acceptable)
        
    -   Dumps (best for production scale)
        

But you are NOT forced to scrape arbitrary public HTML pages.

There is a huge difference between:

> ❌ scraping random user-facing HTML  
> ✅ consuming MediaWiki’s structured REST or Action API output

You should **never scrape `/wiki/...` HTML directly**.

Use:

-   `/w/rest.php/v1/page/...`
    
-   `/w/api.php?action=parse`
    
-   or dumps
    

---

```
Code

input: "έγραψε"  
  
→ try en.wiktionary REST  
    if exists → extract  
    if not → fallback to other edition (rare)  
  
→ detect ==Greek== section  
→ extract POS block  
→ detect "form of" template  
→ map to lemma

```

ChatGPT: 

Here’s a **concrete example of the *raw wikitext template* that is used for *έγραψε*** on the English Wiktionary — this shows the exact template call that your parser would need to recognize and interpret.

In the *Modern Greek* guidelines, the entry for *έγραψε* looks something like this:

-   the definition line uses the **el-form-of-verb** template:
    

```
Code

\# {{el-form-of-verb|γράφω|pers=3s|tense=past}}
```

Here’s what that means in raw Wiktionary wikitext:

```
wikitext

\==Greek==  
\===Verb===  
{{el-form-of-verb|γράφω|pers=3s|tense=past}}  
\# third-person singular simple past of ''\[\[γράφω\]\]'' (gráfo)
```

This line is present in the *non-lemma inflected form* entry and acts as the core structural anchor for your extraction logic. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AAbout_Greek/2007-_version?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### 📌 What this template does

This template call:

```
Code

{{el-form-of-verb|γράφω|pers=3s|tense=past}}
```

carries structured information:

-   **base lemma**: `γράφω`
    
-   **person**: 3rd person (`pers=3s`)
    
-   **tense**: past (`tense=past`)
    

Your extractor needs to parse the template parameters — which, for Greek, are fairly consistent — to recover the core morphosyntactic information from an inflected form. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AAbout_Greek/2007-_version?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## 🔧 Example of expanded template logic

This one line in wikitext encodes:

| Template parameter | Value | Semantic meaning |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `γράφω` | lemma | the base verb |
| `pers=3s` | 3rd person singular | grammatical person/number |
| `tense=past` | past | morphological tense |

Your parser can convert this into a structured JSON or YAML object like:

```
YAML

inflected\_form:  
  lemma: "γράφω"  
  person: "3"  
  number: "singular"  
  tense: "past"
```

---

## 🧠 Why it matters

These *template calls* are precisely what you should aim to target with your extraction logic because:

1.  They are **consistent machine-readable patterns** in the wikitext. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AAbout_Greek/2007-_version?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
2.  They link inflected forms directly to lemmas. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AAbout_Greek/2007-_version?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
3.  They replace the need to scrape prose definitions by humans (e.g., “third-person …”) which are less reliable for parsing.
    

---

## 🧩 What your parser would need to support

For *έγραψε* in Modern Greek, you’ll need to support at least:

-   `el-form-of-verb` (all relevant parameters)
    
-   Standard POS section detection (`==Greek==`, `===Verb===`)
    
-   Extraction of quoted lemma links (`[[γράφω]]`)
    
-   Numerical parsing of person/number/tense features
    

Once you’ve built that **template matcher**, you can reliably generalize across many Greek verb forms. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AAbout_Greek/2007-_version?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# 1️⃣ INFLECTED FORM — έγραψε

Your model is good, but we need two refinements:

-   Separate **derived morphological analysis (your own)** from **attested Wiktionary data**
    
-   Avoid duplicating lemma-level information in the inflected entry
    

Here is a slightly hardened version:

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:έγραψε"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "έγραψε"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ˈeɣrapse/"  
    hyphenation: "έ-γρα-ψε"  
  
  lemma:  
    form: "γράφω"  
    pos: "verb"  
  
  features:  
    person: 3  
    number: "singular"  
    tense: "aorist"  
    voice: "active"  
    mood: "indicative"  
  
  morphology:  
    augment: "έ-"  
    aorist\_marker: "ψ"  
    stem: "γραφ- → γραψ-"  
    ending: "-ε"  
  
  usage:  
    - el: "Έγραψε ένα γράμμα."  
      en: "He/she wrote a letter."
```

### Why this structure is stronger:

-   `features` = grammatical features from Wiktionary template
    
-   `morphology` = your deeper linguistic analysis (stem alternation)
    
-   `lemma` is an object (future-proof if you add lemma IDs)
    

---

# 2️⃣ LEXEME — γράφω

For lemmas, we should distinguish:

-   canonical headword
    
-   inflectional paradigm anchor
    
-   derivational family
    

Refined schema:

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:γράφω"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "γράφω"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ˈɣra.fo/"  
    hyphenation: "γρά‧φω"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "verb"  
  class: "omega\_verb"  
  voice\_type: "active"  
  
  morphology:  
    present\_stem: "γραφ-"  
    aorist\_stem: "γραψ-"  
    augment: "έ-"  
    ending: "-ω"  
  
  paradigm:  
    present\_1sg: "γράφω"  
    aorist\_1sg: "έγραψα"  
    aorist\_3sg: "έγραψε"  
    imperfect\_3sg: "έγραφε"  
    passive\_present: "γράφομαι"  
    passive\_aorist: "γράφτηκα"  
  
  translations:  
    en:  
      - gloss: "to write"  
      - gloss: "to record"  
      - gloss: "to issue (a ticket)"  
  
  derivations:  
    - "γραφή"  
    - "γράμμα"  
    - "γραφικός"  
    - "συγγραφέας"
```

# 🧠 Core Strategy

You only need to support:

1.  **Headword templates (lemma detection)**
    
2.  **Form-of templates (inflected → lemma mapping)**
    
3.  **Inflection-table templates (paradigm extraction)**
    
4.  **Pronunciation template**
    
5.  (Optional) Etymology marker
    

Everything else is decorative.

---

# 1️⃣ VERBS (Modern Greek)

## A. Headword (lemma) templates

You must support:

```
Code

{{el-verb}}  
{{el-verb|γράφω}}
```

These define:

-   POS = verb
    
-   canonical form
    
-   inflection class (sometimes embedded)
    

This alone covers almost all verb lemmas.

---

## B. Inflected-form templates (CRITICAL)

For 90% of verb form pages:

```
Code

{{el-form-of-verb|γράφω|...}}
```

This is your main mapping anchor.

Parameters may encode:

-   person
    
-   number
    
-   tense
    
-   mood
    
-   voice
    

Even if formatting varies slightly, this template is your structural invariant.

If you support this template well, you cover nearly all verb inflected entries.

---

## C. Conjugation table template

On lemma pages you’ll see:

```
Code

{{el-conj-...}}
```

Variants exist, but all conjugation tables are template-driven.

You do NOT need to fully parse the visual table.  
You only need to:

-   detect conjugation template
    
-   optionally extract forms from generated HTML
    
-   or ignore if not building full paradigm
    

For MVP you can skip table parsing.

---

# 2️⃣ NOUNS

After verbs, nouns are next priority.

## A. Headword template

```
Code

{{el-noun}}
```

Encodes:

-   gender
    
-   genitive form
    
-   plural form
    

This one template gives you:

-   lemma
    
-   gender
    
-   declension hints
    

Covers majority of nouns.

---

## B. Inflected-form template

```
Code

{{el-form-of-noun|lemma|...}}
```

Maps case/number to lemma.

This is the noun equivalent of `el-form-of-verb`.

If you support this, you cover almost all noun inflected forms.

---

## C. Declension table template

```
Code

{{el-decl-...}}
```

Optional for MVP.

---

# 3️⃣ ADJECTIVES

## A. Headword template

```
Code

{{el-adj}}
```

Encodes:

-   masculine/feminine/neuter endings
    

This is structurally consistent.

---

## B. Form-of template

```
Code

{{el-form-of-adj|lemma|...}}
```

Encodes:

-   case
    
-   gender
    
-   number
    

Very similar pattern to noun.

---

# 4️⃣ ADVERBS

Adverbs are simpler.

Usually:

```
Code

{{el-adv}}
```

Often no inflection.  
Minimal complexity.

---

# 5️⃣ PARTICIPLES

These often behave like adjectives.

Sometimes:

```
Code

{{el-part}}
```

You can treat them like adjectives initially.

---

# 6️⃣ PRONUNCIATION

Almost universal:

```
Code

{{IPA|el|/.../}}
```

This is language-agnostic.

Support this template once → works for all POS.

---

# 7️⃣ Etymology

Optional:

```
Code

{{der|el|...}}  
{{inh|el|...}}
```

You can ignore etymology for MVP.

---

# 🎯 Minimal Template Support for 90% Coverage

If I were building your extractor, I would initially support:

### Core extraction templates

```
Code

el-verb  
el-form-of-verb  
el-noun  
el-form-of-noun  
el-adj  
el-form-of-adj  
el-adv  
IPA
```

That’s it.

Eight template families.

That alone gets you:

-   lemma detection
    
-   inflected-form mapping
    
-   grammatical features
    
-   IPA
    
-   POS
    
-   gender (for nouns)
    
-   case/number (for nouns/adjectives)
    
-   person/tense/voice/mood (for verbs)
    

This is genuinely enough for ~90% of Modern Greek lookups.

---

# 🚀 Should You Continue with Nouns Next?

Yes.

Correct order:

1.  Verbs (most complex)
    
2.  Nouns (very systematic in Greek)
    
3.  Adjectives (inherit noun logic)
    
4.  Participles
    
5.  Adverbs (easy)
    
6.  Function words (articles, pronouns)
    

---

# 🧩 Architectural Advice

Do NOT build POS-specific parsers.

Build a generic:

```
Code

extractHeadTemplate()  
extractFormOfTemplate()  
extractIPA()  
extractDefinitions()
```

Then map template name → POS-specific feature decoder.

---

# 🧠 Deep Insight

The complexity of Wiktionary is not in parsing text.

It is in normalizing linguistic variation into your ontology.

Your schema is already cleaner than Wiktionary’s.

---

If you want next, we can:

-   Design a unified **Greek grammatical feature ontology**
    
-   Or define the exact template parameter parsing logic for `el-form-of-verb`
    
-   Or define a cross-POS feature matrix (so verbs, nouns, adjectives share one feature model)
    

Which direction do you want to formalize next?

```
YAML
entry:

  id: "el:γράφω"
  language: "el"

  type: "LEXEME"
  form: "γράφω"

  pronunciation:
    IPA: "/ˈɣra.fo/"
  
  hyphenation: "γρά‧φω"

  part_of_speech: "verb"
  class: "verb.act.ω"
  voice_type: "active"

    aorist_stem: "γραψ-"
    augment: "έ-"
    ending: "-ω"

  paradigm:

    aorist_1sg: "έγραψα"
    imperfect_3sg: "έγραφε"

    - "γράμμα"
    - "γραφικός"
    - "συγγραφέας"
```

Given that example, please give me similar templates/schemas/examples for non-lemma verb forms (e.g. έγραψε), lemma-form nouns (e.g. "σπίτι"), non-lemma (= inclined) nouns (e.g. "του σπιτιού"), adjectives (both lemma- and non-lemma forms), participles (both lemma- and non-lemma forms), adverbs, and function words (articles, pronouns — each lemma and non-lemma forms).

ChatGPT: 

Below are **parallel YAML output templates** in the same style as your **γράφω** example. I’m keeping them **schema-consistent** across POS, with a few POS-specific fields.

I’ll use one representative example per category (lemma + non-lemma where applicable).

---

## 0) Shared conventions (applies to all)

```
YAML

\# entry.id pattern suggestions:  
\#  - lemma: "el:<FORM>"  
\#  - inflected: "el:<FORM>#<FEATURES\_KEY>"   (stable, deterministic)  
\# entry.type values:  
\#  - LEXEME | INFLECTED\_FORM
```

---

# 1) Verb — non-lemma (e.g. έγραψε)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:έγραψε#verb.aor.ind.act.3sg"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "έγραψε"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ˈeɣrapse/"  
  hyphenation: "έ-γρα-ψε"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:γράφω"  
    form: "γράφω"  
    part\_of\_speech: "verb"  
    class: "verb.act.ω"  
  
  features:  
    tense: "aorist"  
    mood: "indicative"  
    voice: "active"  
    person: 3  
    number: "singular"  
  
  morphology:  
    augment: "έ-"  
    stem: "γραψ-"  
    ending: "-ε"  
  
  usage:  
    - el: "Έγραψε ένα γράμμα."  
      en: "He/she wrote a letter."
```

---

# 2) Noun — lemma (e.g. σπίτι)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:σπίτι"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "σπίτι"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ˈspi.ti/"  
  hyphenation: "σπί‧τι"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "noun"  
  gender: "neuter"  
  class: "noun.n.ι"   \# your own declension-family label (example)  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "σπιτ-"  
    ending: "-ι"  
  
  paradigm:  
    nominative\_sg: "σπίτι"  
    genitive\_sg: "σπιτιού"  
    accusative\_sg: "σπίτι"  
    vocative\_sg: "σπίτι"  
    nominative\_pl: "σπίτια"  
    genitive\_pl: "σπιτιών"  
    accusative\_pl: "σπίτια"  
    vocative\_pl: "σπίτια"  
  
  translations:  
    en:  
      - gloss: "house"  
      - gloss: "home"  
  
  derivations:  
    - "σπιτικός"  
    - "σπιτάκι"
```

---

# 3) Noun — non-lemma (inclined; e.g. σπιτιού / “του σπιτιού”)

I recommend: store the **inflected token** (`σπιτιού`) as `form`, and treat surrounding clitics/articles (“του …”) as a **phrase wrapper** you can optionally represent separately.

### 3A) Pure inflected noun token

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:σπιτιού#noun.gen.sg"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "σπιτιού"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/spiˈtçu/"   \# example only; may omit if unavailable  
  hyphenation: "σπι‧τι‧ού"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:σπίτι"  
    form: "σπίτι"  
    part\_of\_speech: "noun"  
    gender: "neuter"  
    class: "noun.n.ι"  
  
  features:  
    case: "genitive"  
    number: "singular"  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "σπιτι-"  
    ending: "-ού"  
  
  usage:  
    - el: "Η πόρτα του σπιτιού είναι κλειστή."  
      en: "The house door is closed."
```

### 3B) Optional: phrase entry (article + noun inflection)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:του σπιτιού#phrase.det+noun.gen.sg"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "PHRASE"  
  form: "του σπιτιού"  
  
  components:  
    - id: "el:ο#art.gen.sg.m"  
      form: "του"  
      role: "definite\_article"  
    - id: "el:σπιτιού#noun.gen.sg"  
      form: "σπιτιού"  
      role: "head\_noun"  
  
  features:  
    case: "genitive"  
    number: "singular"  
    definiteness: "definite"
```

---

# 4) Adjective — lemma (e.g. καλός)

Adjectives are naturally tri-gender + case/number inflection.

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:καλός"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "καλός"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/kaˈlos/"  
  hyphenation: "κα‧λός"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "adjective"  
  class: "adj.ος-η-ο"   \# your adjective family label (example)  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "καλ-"  
  
  paradigm:  
    masculine:  
      nominative\_sg: "καλός"  
      genitive\_sg: "καλού"  
      accusative\_sg: "καλό"  
      nominative\_pl: "καλοί"  
      genitive\_pl: "καλών"  
      accusative\_pl: "καλούς"  
    feminine:  
      nominative\_sg: "καλή"  
      genitive\_sg: "καλής"  
      accusative\_sg: "καλή"  
      nominative\_pl: "καλές"  
      genitive\_pl: "καλών"  
      accusative\_pl: "καλές"  
    neuter:  
      nominative\_sg: "καλό"  
      genitive\_sg: "καλού"  
      accusative\_sg: "καλό"  
      nominative\_pl: "καλά"  
      genitive\_pl: "καλών"  
      accusative\_pl: "καλά"  
  
  translations:  
    en:  
      - gloss: "good"  
      - gloss: "kind; nice"
```

---

# 5) Adjective — non-lemma (e.g. καλού)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:καλού#adj.gen.sg.m|n"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "καλού"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:καλός"  
    form: "καλός"  
    part\_of\_speech: "adjective"  
    class: "adj.ος-η-ο"  
  
  features:  
    case: "genitive"  
    number: "singular"  
    gender: \["masculine", "neuter"\]  \# same surface form fits both  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "καλ-"  
    ending: "-ού"
```

---

# 6) Participle — lemma (example: γραμμένος)

Treat participles as their own POS, but reuse adjective-like inflection.

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:γραμμένος"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "γραμμένος"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/ɣraˈmenos/"  
  hyphenation: "γραμ‧μέ‧νος"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "participle"  
  subtype: "verbal\_adjective"  
  related\_verb\_lemma:  
    id: "el:γράφω"  
    form: "γράφω"  
  
  features:  
    voice: "passive"  
    aspect: "perfective"   \# or "resultative" depending on your ontology  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "γραμ-"  
    suffix: "-μένος"  
  
  paradigm: \# adjective-like  
    masculine\_nom\_sg: "γραμμένος"  
    feminine\_nom\_sg: "γραμμένη"  
    neuter\_nom\_sg: "γραμμένο"
```

---

# 7) Participle — non-lemma (e.g. γραμμένης)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:γραμμένης#ptcp.gen.sg.f"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "γραμμένης"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:γραμμένος"  
    form: "γραμμένος"  
    part\_of\_speech: "participle"  
  
  features:  
    case: "genitive"  
    number: "singular"  
    gender: "feminine"  
  
  morphology:  
    stem: "γραμμ-"  
    ending: "-ης"
```

---

# 8) Adverb — lemma (e.g. καλά)

Most adverbs are invariant.

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:καλά"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "καλά"  
  
  pronunciation:  
    IPA: "/kaˈla/"  
  hyphenation: "κα‧λά"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "adverb"  
  degree: "positive"   \# optional  
  
  related\_to:  
    id: "el:καλός"  
    form: "καλός"  
    relation: "adverb\_of\_adjective"  
  
  translations:  
    en:  
      - gloss: "well"  
      - gloss: "nicely"
```

Non-lemma adverbs usually **don’t exist** (except comparative/superlative forms, which are typically separate lexemes like “καλύτερα”).

---

# 9) Function words

## 9A) Definite article — lemma (ο)

Articles have many forms; treat “ο” as lexeme, all forms as inflected.

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:ο"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "ο"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "article"  
  subtype: "definite"  
  
  paradigm:  
    masculine:  
      nominative\_sg: "ο"  
      genitive\_sg: "του"  
      accusative\_sg: "τον"  
      nominative\_pl: "οι"  
      genitive\_pl: "των"  
      accusative\_pl: "τους"  
    feminine:  
      nominative\_sg: "η"  
      genitive\_sg: "της"  
      accusative\_sg: "την"  
      nominative\_pl: "οι"  
      genitive\_pl: "των"  
      accusative\_pl: "τις"  
    neuter:  
      nominative\_sg: "το"  
      genitive\_sg: "του"  
      accusative\_sg: "το"  
      nominative\_pl: "τα"  
      genitive\_pl: "των"  
      accusative\_pl: "τα"
```

## 9B) Definite article — non-lemma (του)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:του#art.gen.sg.m|n"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "του"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:ο"  
    form: "ο"  
    part\_of\_speech: "article"  
    subtype: "definite"  
  
  features:  
    case: "genitive"  
    number: "singular"  
    gender: \["masculine", "neuter"\]  
  
  role:  
    syntactic: "determiner"
```

---

## 9C) Personal pronoun — lemma (εγώ)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:εγώ"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "LEXEME"  
  form: "εγώ"  
  
  part\_of\_speech: "pronoun"  
  subtype: "personal"  
  person: 1  
  
  paradigm:  
    nominative: "εγώ"  
    genitive: "μου"  
    accusative: "με"  
  
  notes:  
    - "Genitive/accusative forms are clitics in most contexts."
```

## 9D) Personal pronoun — non-lemma (μου)

```
YAML

entry:  
  id: "el:μου#pron.gen.1sg"  
  language: "el"  
  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
  form: "μου"  
  
  lemma:  
    id: "el:εγώ"  
    form: "εγώ"  
    part\_of\_speech: "pronoun"  
    subtype: "personal"  
  
  features:  
    person: 1  
    number: "singular"  
    case: "genitive"  
    clitic: true  
  
  role:  
    syntactic: \["possessive\_determiner", "object\_pronoun"\]  \# context-dependent
```

---

# 10) Notes on “non-lemma” for function words

Many function-word “forms” are not **inflection** but **clitic variants** or **orthographic variants**. Your schema already supports this: represent those as `INFLECTED_FORM` with `clitic: true` or `variant_of`.

---

# Suggested POS expansion order

Yes — after verbs, continue:

1.  **Nouns** (declension, gender, cases)
    
2.  **Adjectives** (reuse noun case/number logic + gender)
    
3.  **Articles** (small but high-frequency paradigm)
    
4.  **Pronouns** (finite paradigms, clitics)
    
5.  **Participles** (adjective-like + verb linkage)
    
6.  **Adverbs** (mostly invariant; handle degree/comparison)
    

This order maximizes early coverage and minimizes new machinery per POS.

---

If you want the next step to be *operational*, I can now:

-   define a **single unified `features` ontology** that works across verb/noun/adj/pron/article
    
-   define `id` canonicalization rules (including Greek normalization + stress handling)
    
-   map each schema field to likely Wiktionary sources (template params vs definition lines vs tables)

You: 

Given these data structures we have come to define now, for most of the parts-of-speech types, inlcuing lemma and non-lemma forms, please propose an implementation plan for building a TypeScript `fetchWiktionary(<query_term>)` function that would call Wiktionary, get the data, parse and structure it in the format(s) as we have discussed. `<query_term>` (of value = string) would obviously always be a required attribute. We could add optional attributes like language (e.g. `lang:"el"`) to help the function select the proper Wiktionary data source, as well as an optional "PoS" attribute, such that we can give disambiguate in cases more than one object can be expected in cases of homonymy.

ChatGPT: 

Below is a concrete implementation plan for a TypeScript `fetchWiktionary(queryTerm, options?)` that returns the **structured `entry` objects** we defined (LEXEME / INFLECTED\_FORM, multiple POS, lemma + non-lemma).

I’m assuming your primary target is **Modern Greek**, but the design supports other languages.

---

## 1) Function shape and return types

### Public API

```
TypeScript

type Pos \=  
  | "verb" | "noun" | "adjective" | "participle" | "adverb"  
  | "article" | "pronoun"  
  | "unknown";  
  
type EntryType \= "LEXEME" | "INFLECTED\_FORM" | "PHRASE";  
  
interface FetchWiktionaryOptions {  
  lang?: string;              // e.g. "el"  
  pos?: Pos;                  // disambiguation hint  
  wiktionaryEdition?: "en" | "el" | "auto";  // default "auto"  
  prefer?: "wikitext" | "html";              // default "wikitext"  
  includeRaw?: boolean;       // attach raw blocks for debugging  
  timeoutMs?: number;  
}  
  
interface FetchWiktionaryResult {  
  query: { input: string; lang?: string; pos?: Pos };  
  candidates: StructuredEntry\[\];  // 0..n; homonyms => multiple  
  warnings?: string\[\];  
  source: { edition: string; pageTitle: string; revisionId?: number };  
}  
  
type StructuredEntry \= /\* your YAML schema mapped to TS \*/;
```

### Key decision: return **candidates\[\]**, not a single entry

Because homonymy and multi-POS entries are common. You can still provide `pos` to filter to one.

---

## 2) Data source strategy (domains & endpoints)

### Recommended default edition selection

-   If `options.wiktionaryEdition === "en"` → always query **en.wiktionary.org**.
    
-   If `"el"` → query **el.wiktionary.org** (but coverage may be lower).
    
-   If `"auto"` (default):
    
    1.  Try `lang === "el"` → **en.wiktionary first** (best coverage for Greek)
        
    2.  Optionally fallback to `el.wiktionary` only if you explicitly want it (rare)
        

### Endpoint choice

Prefer **Action API wikitext** as primary because:

-   stable for parsing templates
    
-   you need template calls for form-of/lemma mapping
    

Use:

-   **Parse page** (gives wikitext + sections + template list):
    
    -   `GET https://en.wiktionary.org/w/api.php?action=parse&page=<TITLE>&prop=wikitext|sections|templates&format=json&formatversion=2&origin=*`
        

Fallbacks:

-   If `action=parse` fails (rare) → `action=query&prop=revisions&rvprop=content`
    
-   If you want HTML fallback → `action=parse&prop=text` (parsed HTML)
    

**Do not** scrape `/wiki/<TITLE>`.

---

## 3) High-level pipeline

### `fetchWiktionary(queryTerm, opts)` steps

1.  **Normalize queryTerm** (lightweight)
    
    -   trim
        
    -   keep original for output
        
    -   for Greek: normalize Unicode (NFC), optionally remove surrounding punctuation
        
    -   compute `encodedTitle = encodeURIComponent(term)`
        
2.  **Fetch page via Action API**
    
    -   call `action=parse`
        
    -   handle “page does not exist” gracefully
        
    -   store `wikitext` (string), `sections` (array), `templates` (array)
        
3.  **Split into language blocks**
    
    -   locate the `==Greek==` block if `lang:"el"` (or map languages → section titles)
        
    -   if `lang` not provided: detect languages present and return multiple (optional)
        
4.  **Within language block, split into POS blocks**
    
    -   headings like `===Verb===`, `===Noun===`, etc.
        
    -   for Greek on en.wiktionary, POS headings are fairly consistent
        
5.  **Extract per POS block**
    
    -   headword template(s) → lemma detection
        
    -   form-of template(s) → inflected detection + lemma link + features
        
    -   IPA from `{{IPA|...}}` occurrences in Pronunciation subsection if present
        
    -   hyphenation if present (often via templates; else skip)
        
    -   translations from Translation subsection (lemma entries only; optional MVP)
        
    -   derivations/derived terms (optional MVP)
        
6.  **Classify into your entry objects**
    
    -   if contains `el-form-of-*` template → `INFLECTED_FORM`
        
    -   else if contains `el-verb`/`el-noun`/`el-adj`/etc → `LEXEME`
        
    -   else → `type:"LEXEME"` with `pos:"unknown"` (or skip)
        
7.  **Disambiguation**
    
    -   if `opts.pos` provided: filter candidates to matching POS
        
    -   if `opts.lang` provided: only that language block
        
    -   otherwise return all candidates found
        
8.  **Optional enrichment passes**
    
    -   If `INFLECTED_FORM` and you want lemma details: optionally fetch lemma page and attach `lemma` object (or just lemma id/form)
        
    -   This should be opt-in (`opts.expandLemma?: boolean`) because it doubles calls.
        
9.  **Return `FetchWiktionaryResult`**
    

---

## 4) Parsing approach: “template-extractor”, not full wikitext parser

You don’t need a full MediaWiki parser. For 90% coverage, you need:

### Minimal template set (Greek MVP)

-   `el-verb`, `el-noun`, `el-adj`, `el-adv`, `el-part` (lemma signals)
    
-   `el-form-of-verb`, `el-form-of-noun`, `el-form-of-adj` (inflected signals)
    
-   `IPA` (pronunciation)
    

### Implementation technique

Use a **shallow scanner** that:

-   finds `{{...}}` template invocations
    
-   parses the template name + pipe-separated params
    
-   ignores nested templates initially (support later)
    

A robust-enough template parser for MVP:

-   iterate char-by-char
    
-   detect `{{`
    
-   parse until matching `}}` accounting for nested `{{ }}` depth
    
-   extract raw inside string, then split on `|` at depth 0 (not inside nested)
    

This gives you structured `TemplateCall`:

```
TypeScript

interface TemplateCall {  
  name: string;           // e.g. "el-form-of-verb"  
  args: string\[\];         // positional args  
  kwargs: Record<string,string\>; // key=value params  
  raw: string;  
  start: number;  
  end: number;  
}
```

Then you write small decoders:

-   `decodeElFormOfVerb(call)` → `{ lemma: "γράφω", features: {...}}`
    
-   `decodeElNoun(call)` → `{ gender, genitive, plural }` (where possible)
    
-   `decodeIPA(call, lang)` → IPA string(s)
    

---

## 5) How to map “features” across POS

Define a single union-friendly feature object:

```
TypeScript

interface Features {  
  // shared  
  number?: "singular" | "plural";  
  gender?: "masculine" | "feminine" | "neuter" | ("masculine"|"feminine"|"neuter")\[\];  
  case?: "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative";  
  
  // verbs  
  person?: 1|2|3;  
  tense?: "present" | "aorist" | "imperfect" | "future" | string;  
  mood?: "indicative" | "subjunctive" | "imperative" | string;  
  voice?: "active" | "middle" | "passive" | string;  
  
  // function words  
  definiteness?: "definite" | "indefinite";  
  clitic?: boolean;  
}
```

Your schema stays stable; only the decoder logic differs per POS/template.

---

## 6) Homonymy / multiple outputs

When a page has multiple POS (very common), you’ll return:

```
TypeScript

{  
  candidates: \[  
    { entry: { part\_of\_speech: "noun", ... } },  
    { entry: { part\_of\_speech: "verb", ... } }  
  \]  
}
```

Then `opts.pos` becomes a filter/hint.

Also: a single token may have **multiple analyses** (e.g. “καλού” m/n). That becomes one entry with `gender: ["masculine","neuter"]`.

---

## 7) Optional: phrase handling (“του σπιτιού”)

If `queryTerm` contains whitespace:

-   Attempt **direct page lookup** first (some phrases exist)
    
-   Else run a **tokenizer**:
    
    -   split on whitespace
        
    -   fetch each token as separate entry
        
    -   build `PHRASE` entry with components (as we sketched)
        

This is extremely useful in Greek because many learners paste “του X”.

---

## 8) Engineering checklist

### HTTP & politeness

-   Use `origin=*` for CORS in browser
    
-   Set a descriptive `User-Agent` (server-side Node): Wikimedia wants that
    
-   Add basic rate limiting + in-memory cache
    

### Caching

-   `Map<string, CachedResult>` keyed by `edition|title|lang|pos`
    
-   TTL (e.g. 24h) because Wiktionary changes slowly for most entries
    

### Testing

-   Golden test fixtures: store wikitext snapshots for key words
    
-   Unit tests per decoder: `el-form-of-verb`, `el-noun`, `IPA`, etc.
    

### Telemetry

-   `warnings[]` field: missing Greek block, missing templates, ambiguous parsing
    

---

## 9) Milestone plan (practical)

### Milestone 1 — Core retrieval + Greek verbs (1–2 days of work)

-   fetch wikitext via `action=parse`
    
-   parse templates (nested-safe)
    
-   support: `el-form-of-verb`, `el-verb`, `IPA`
    
-   output: verb lemma + verb inflected
    

### Milestone 2 — Nouns + adjectives (coverage jump)

-   add: `el-noun`, `el-form-of-noun`, `el-adj`, `el-form-of-adj`
    
-   add `case/number/gender` mapping
    
-   optional: hyphenation if present
    

### Milestone 3 — Articles + pronouns (function words)

-   treat as paradigms; decode lemma pages + inflected forms
    
-   add clitic handling
    

### Milestone 4 — Translations + derived terms

-   parse “Translations” blocks (this is the messier part)
    
-   start with English gloss list only
    

### Milestone 5 — Lemma enrichment

-   allow `expandLemma: true` that fetches lemma when starting from inflected form
    

---

## 10) Suggested API (ergonomic)

```
TypeScript

const r \= await fetchWiktionary("έγραψε", { lang: "el", pos: "verb", expandLemma: true });  
  
r.candidates\[0\].entry.type \=== "INFLECTED\_FORM"  
r.candidates\[0\].entry.lemma.form \=== "γράφω"
```
