…and we can iterate from there.

You: 

Great! Go ahead starting to implement all and everything!

ChatGPT: 

```
TypeScript

/\* ============================================================================  
Wiktionary Fetch + Parse (TypeScript) — MVP implementation  
\- Uses MediaWiki Action API (action=parse) to fetch wikitext + sections + templates  
\- Extracts structured entries for Modern Greek (lang="el") from en.wiktionary.org  
\- Supports lemma + inflected forms for:  
  verbs, nouns, adjectives, participles (basic), adverbs (basic), articles (basic), pronouns (basic)  
  
Design goals:  
\- No scraping of /wiki HTML  
\- No full wikitext parser; instead: a shallow template extractor + section slicer  
\- Extensible template decoder registry  
  
You can drop this into a package as \`src/wiktionary.ts\`.  
\============================================================================ \*/  
  
export type WiktionaryEdition \= "en" | "el" | "auto";  
export type EntryType \= "LEXEME" | "INFLECTED\_FORM" | "PHRASE";  
export type Pos \=  
  | "verb"  
  | "noun"  
  | "adjective"  
  | "participle"  
  | "adverb"  
  | "article"  
  | "pronoun"  
  | "unknown";  
  
export interface FetchWiktionaryOptions {  
  lang?: string; // e.g. "el"  
  pos?: Pos; // disambiguation hint  
  edition?: WiktionaryEdition; // default "auto"  
  prefer?: "wikitext" | "html"; // default "wikitext"  
  includeRaw?: boolean; // attach raw blocks for debugging  
  expandLemma?: boolean; // if query is inflected: fetch lemma page too (extra call)  
  timeoutMs?: number; // default 15\_000  
  cacheTtlMs?: number; // default 24h  
}  
  
export interface FetchWiktionaryResult {  
  query: { input: string; lang?: string; pos?: Pos };  
  candidates: StructuredEntry\[\];  
  warnings: string\[\];  
  source: {  
    edition: string;  
    pageTitle: string;  
    revisionId?: number;  
    fetchedAt: string;  
  };  
}  
  
export type Gender \= "masculine" | "feminine" | "neuter";  
export type GrCase \= "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative";  
export type GrNumber \= "singular" | "plural";  
  
export type VerbTense \= "present" | "aorist" | "imperfect" | "future" | string;  
export type VerbMood \= "indicative" | "subjunctive" | "imperative" | string;  
export type VerbVoice \= "active" | "middle" | "passive" | string;  
  
export interface Features {  
  // shared  
  number?: GrNumber;  
  gender?: Gender | Gender\[\];  
  case?: GrCase;  
  
  // verbs  
  person?: 1 | 2 | 3;  
  tense?: VerbTense;  
  mood?: VerbMood;  
  voice?: VerbVoice;  
  
  // function words  
  definiteness?: "definite" | "indefinite";  
  clitic?: boolean;  
  
  // extra  
  \[k: string\]: unknown;  
}  
  
export interface Pronunciation {  
  IPA?: string | string\[\];  
  // future: audio urls, phonetic respellings, etc.  
}  
  
export interface LemmaRef {  
  id?: string;  
  form: string;  
  part\_of\_speech?: Pos;  
  class?: string;  
  gender?: Gender;  
  subtype?: string;  
}  
  
export interface BaseEntry {  
  id: string;  
  language: string; // BCP-47-ish tag (here: "el")  
  type: EntryType;  
  form: string;  
  part\_of\_speech?: Pos;  
  pronunciation?: Pronunciation;  
  hyphenation?: string;  
  
  // debug / introspection  
  \_raw?: {  
    edition: string;  
    pageTitle: string;  
    wikitextSlice?: string;  
    templates?: TemplateCall\[\];  
    posHeading?: string;  
  };  
}  
  
export interface LexemeEntry extends BaseEntry {  
  type: "LEXEME";  
  class?: string;  
  voice\_type?: string; // verbs/participles etc  
  gender?: Gender; // nouns  
  morphology?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  paradigm?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  translations?: Record<string, Array<{ gloss: string }>>;  
  derivations?: string\[\];  
}  
  
export interface InflectedEntry extends BaseEntry {  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM";  
  lemma: LemmaRef;  
  features: Features;  
  morphology?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  usage?: Array<Record<string, string\>>;  
}  
  
export interface PhraseEntry extends BaseEntry {  
  type: "PHRASE";  
  components: Array<{  
    id?: string;  
    form: string;  
    role?: string;  
  }>;  
  features?: Features;  
}  
  
export type StructuredEntry \= LexemeEntry | InflectedEntry | PhraseEntry;  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
MediaWiki API types (action=parse)  
\============================================================================ \*/  
type MWParseResponse \= {  
  parse?: {  
    title: string;  
    pageid: number;  
    revid?: number;  
    wikitext?: string | { "\*": string };  
    sections?: Array<{  
      toclevel: number;  
      level: string;  
      line: string;  
      number: string;  
      index: string;  
      fromtitle: string;  
      byteoffset: number;  
      anchor: string;  
    }>;  
    templates?: Array<{ "\*": string }>;  
  };  
  error?: { code: string; info: string };  
};  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Caching  
\============================================================================ \*/  
type CacheItem<T\> \= { value: T; expiresAt: number };  
const memCache \= new Map<string, CacheItem<any\>>();  
  
function cacheGet<T\>(key: string): T | undefined {  
  const it \= memCache.get(key);  
  if (!it) return undefined;  
  if (Date.now() \> it.expiresAt) {  
    memCache.delete(key);  
    return undefined;  
  }  
  return it.value as T;  
}  
  
function cacheSet<T\>(key: string, value: T, ttlMs: number) {  
  memCache.set(key, { value, expiresAt: Date.now() + ttlMs });  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Public entry point  
\============================================================================ \*/  
export async function fetchWiktionary(  
  queryTerm: string,  
  options: FetchWiktionaryOptions \= {}  
): Promise<FetchWiktionaryResult\> {  
  const warnings: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  const timeoutMs \= options.timeoutMs ?? 15\_000;  
  const cacheTtlMs \= options.cacheTtlMs ?? 24 \* 60 \* 60 \* 1000;  
  
  const normalized \= normalizeQuery(queryTerm);  
  if (!normalized) {  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings: \["Empty query term after normalization."\],  
      source: { edition: "n/a", pageTitle: "", fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  // Phrase handling: optional.  
  if (/\\s/.test(normalized)) {  
    const phraseRes \= await tryPhrase(normalized, options, warnings);  
    if (phraseRes) return phraseRes;  
  }  
  
  const edition \= chooseEdition(options);  
  const domain \= edition \=== "el" ? "el.wiktionary.org" : "en.wiktionary.org";  
  
  const parse \= await fetchParsePage(domain, normalized, timeoutMs, cacheTtlMs, warnings);  
  
  if (!parse.parse?.wikitext) {  
    const info \= parse.error?.info ?? "No parse data returned.";  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings: \[...warnings, info\],  
      source: {  
        edition,  
        pageTitle: parse.parse?.title ?? normalized,  
        revisionId: parse.parse?.revid,  
        fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString(),  
      },  
    };  
  }  
  
  const wikitext \= typeof parse.parse.wikitext \=== "string" ? parse.parse.wikitext : parse.parse.wikitext\["\*"\];  
  const pageTitle \= parse.parse.title ?? normalized;  
  const revisionId \= parse.parse.revid;  
  
  // Extract language block(s)  
  const lang \= options.lang ?? "el";  
  const langBlock \= extractLanguageBlock(wikitext, lang, warnings);  
  
  if (!langBlock) {  
    // If user didn't force lang, we could return all langs; here we just warn.  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings: \[...warnings, \`No language block found for lang="${lang}".\`\],  
      source: { edition, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  // Split into POS blocks  
  const posBlocks \= splitPosBlocks(langBlock.text);  
  
  // Parse templates once per POS block (keeps scopes tighter)  
  const candidates: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const block of posBlocks) {  
    const pos \= mapPosHeadingToPos(block.heading);  
    if (options.pos && options.pos !== pos) continue;  
  
    const templates \= parseTemplates(block.text);  
    const pron \= extractPronunciation(block.text, lang);  
  
    const decoded \= decodeBlock({  
      lang,  
      pageTitle,  
      edition,  
      posHeading: block.heading,  
      blockText: block.text,  
      templates,  
      pronunciation: pron,  
      includeRaw: !!options.includeRaw,  
    });  
  
    for (const e of decoded) candidates.push(e);  
  }  
  
  // Heuristic: if no POS blocks found, try whole language block as one unknown block  
  if (candidates.length \=== 0) {  
    const templates \= parseTemplates(langBlock.text);  
    const pron \= extractPronunciation(langBlock.text, lang);  
    const decoded \= decodeBlock({  
      lang,  
      pageTitle,  
      edition,  
      posHeading: "UNKNOWN",  
      blockText: langBlock.text,  
      templates,  
      pronunciation: pron,  
      includeRaw: !!options.includeRaw,  
    });  
    candidates.push(...decoded);  
  }  
  
  // Optional lemma expansion for inflected forms  
  if (options.expandLemma) {  
    await expandLemmaForInflected(candidates, options, warnings);  
  }  
  
  return {  
    query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
    candidates,  
    warnings,  
    source: { edition, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Edition selection  
\============================================================================ \*/  
function chooseEdition(options: FetchWiktionaryOptions): "en" | "el" {  
  const ed \= options.edition ?? "auto";  
  if (ed \=== "en") return "en";  
  if (ed \=== "el") return "el";  
  // auto: for Greek lexicographic coverage, default to en.wiktionary  
  // (You can later implement a “try el then en” strategy if you prefer.)  
  return "en";  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
HTTP fetch helpers  
\============================================================================ \*/  
async function fetchParsePage(  
  domain: string,  
  title: string,  
  timeoutMs: number,  
  cacheTtlMs: number,  
  warnings: string\[\]  
): Promise<MWParseResponse\> {  
  const cacheKey \= \`parse:${domain}:${title}\`;  
  const cached \= cacheGet<MWParseResponse\>(cacheKey);  
  if (cached) return cached;  
  
  const url \=  
    \`https://${domain}/w/api.php\` +  
    \`?action=parse\` +  
    \`&page=${encodeURIComponent(title)}\` +  
    \`&prop=wikitext|sections|templates\` +  
    \`&format=json\` +  
    \`&formatversion=2\` +  
    \`&origin=\*\`;  
  
  const res \= await fetchWithTimeout(url, timeoutMs);  
  if (!res.ok) {  
    warnings.push(\`HTTP ${res.status} ${res.statusText} for action=parse.\`);  
    const text \= await safeReadText(res);  
    return { error: { code: "http\_error", info: text || res.statusText } };  
  }  
  
  const json \= (await res.json()) as MWParseResponse;  
  if (json.error) warnings.push(\`MediaWiki error: ${json.error.code}: ${json.error.info}\`);  
  
  cacheSet(cacheKey, json, cacheTtlMs);  
  return json;  
}  
  
async function fetchWithTimeout(url: string, timeoutMs: number): Promise<Response\> {  
  const controller \= new AbortController();  
  const t \= setTimeout(() => controller.abort(), timeoutMs);  
  try {  
    return await fetch(url, { signal: controller.signal });  
  } finally {  
    clearTimeout(t);  
  }  
}  
  
async function safeReadText(res: Response): Promise<string\> {  
  try {  
    return await res.text();  
  } catch {  
    return "";  
  }  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Normalization & phrase handling  
\============================================================================ \*/  
function normalizeQuery(s: string): string {  
  return (s ?? "")  
    .trim()  
    .normalize("NFC");  
}  
  
async function tryPhrase(  
  phrase: string,  
  options: FetchWiktionaryOptions,  
  warnings: string\[\]  
): Promise<FetchWiktionaryResult | null\> {  
  // Strategy:  
  // 1) Attempt direct lookup (sometimes a phrase exists as a page)  
  // 2) If not found / no candidates, tokenize and return PHRASE with component entries  
  const direct \= await fetchWiktionary(phrase, { ...options, // avoid infinite recursion with phrase check  
    // Temporarily disable phrase retry by stripping spaces? We'll just allow direct call  
    // but if it loops, protect:  
    // (we’ll just do a direct parse call here to avoid recursion)  
  }).catch(() => null);  
  
  if (direct && direct.candidates.length \> 0) return direct;  
  
  // Tokenize  
  const tokens \= phrase.split(/\\s+/).filter(Boolean);  
  if (tokens.length <= 1) return null;  
  
  const componentEntries: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const tok of tokens) {  
    const r \= await fetchWiktionary(tok, { ...options, expandLemma: false }).catch(() => null);  
    if (r?.candidates?.length) componentEntries.push(...r.candidates);  
  }  
  
  const phraseEntry: PhraseEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${phrase}#phrase\`,  
    language: options.lang ?? "el",  
    type: "PHRASE",  
    form: phrase,  
    part\_of\_speech: "unknown",  
    components: tokens.map((t) => ({ form: t })),  
  };  
  
  return {  
    query: { input: phrase, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
    candidates: \[phraseEntry, ...componentEntries\],  
    warnings: \[...warnings, "Phrase not found as page; returned tokenized PHRASE + component entries."\],  
    source: { edition: chooseEdition(options), pageTitle: phrase, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Language block extraction  
\============================================================================ \*/  
function extractLanguageBlock(  
  wikitext: string,  
  lang: string,  
  warnings: string\[\]  
): { heading: string; text: string } | null {  
  // For en.wiktionary, language headings are like: ==Greek==  
  // Map lang codes to Wiktionary language names (extend as needed)  
  const langName \= langCodeToWiktionaryLanguageName(lang);  
  if (!langName) {  
    warnings.push(\`Unknown lang mapping for "${lang}".\`);  
    return null;  
  }  
  
  const re \= new RegExp(\`^==\\\\s\*${escapeRegex(langName)}\\\\s\*==\\\\s\*$\`, "m");  
  const m \= re.exec(wikitext);  
  if (!m) return null;  
  
  const start \= m.index;  
  // Find next language heading "==...=="  
  const after \= wikitext.slice(start + m\[0\].length);  
  const next \= after.search(/^==\[^=\].\*==\\s\*$/m);  
  const end \= next \=== \-1 ? wikitext.length : start + m\[0\].length + next;  
  
  return { heading: langName, text: wikitext.slice(start, end) };  
}  
  
function langCodeToWiktionaryLanguageName(lang: string): string | null {  
  switch (lang) {  
    case "el":  
      return "Greek";  
    case "nl":  
      return "Dutch";  
    case "en":  
      return "English";  
    case "de":  
      return "German";  
    case "fr":  
      return "French";  
    default:  
      return null;  
  }  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
POS block splitting  
\============================================================================ \*/  
type PosBlock \= { heading: string; text: string };  
  
function splitPosBlocks(langBlockText: string): PosBlock\[\] {  
  // POS headings are typically "===Verb===" etc.  
  // We'll split on ^===...=== lines within the language block.  
  const lines \= langBlockText.split("\\n");  
  const blocks: PosBlock\[\] \= \[\];  
  let currentHeading \= "LANG\_BLOCK";  
  let buf: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  
  const headingRe \= /^===\\s\*(\[^=\].\*?)\\s\*===\\s\*$/;  
  
  for (const line of lines) {  
    const hm \= headingRe.exec(line);  
    if (hm) {  
      if (buf.length) blocks.push({ heading: currentHeading, text: buf.join("\\n") });  
      currentHeading \= hm\[1\].trim();  
      buf \= \[line\];  
    } else {  
      buf.push(line);  
    }  
  }  
  if (buf.length) blocks.push({ heading: currentHeading, text: buf.join("\\n") });  
  
  // Drop the initial "LANG\_BLOCK" if it has no meaningful content besides the ==Greek== line  
  return blocks.filter((b) => b.text.trim().length \> 0);  
}  
  
function mapPosHeadingToPos(h: string): Pos {  
  const x \= h.toLowerCase();  
  if (x.includes("verb")) return "verb";  
  if (x.includes("noun")) return "noun";  
  if (x.includes("adjective")) return "adjective";  
  if (x.includes("participle")) return "participle";  
  if (x.includes("adverb")) return "adverb";  
  if (x.includes("article")) return "article";  
  if (x.includes("pronoun")) return "pronoun";  
  return "unknown";  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Template parsing  
\============================================================================ \*/  
export interface TemplateCall {  
  name: string;  
  args: string\[\];  
  kwargs: Record<string, string\>;  
  raw: string; // inside braces  
  start: number;  
  end: number;  
}  
  
function parseTemplates(text: string): TemplateCall\[\] {  
  const calls: TemplateCall\[\] \= \[\];  
  let i \= 0;  
  
  while (i < text.length) {  
    const open \= text.indexOf("{{", i);  
    if (open \=== \-1) break;  
  
    // scan to matching "}}", tracking nesting  
    let depth \= 0;  
    let j \= open;  
    let in \= "";  
    while (j < text.length) {  
      if (text.startsWith("{{", j)) {  
        depth++;  
        j += 2;  
        continue;  
      }  
      if (text.startsWith("}}", j)) {  
        depth\--;  
        j += 2;  
        if (depth \=== 0) break;  
        continue;  
      }  
      // accumulate content only for outermost template (depth>=1)  
      if (depth \>= 1) in += text\[j\];  
      j++;  
    }  
  
    if (depth !== 0) {  
      // unbalanced, stop  
      break;  
    }  
  
    // \`in\` includes content from \*all\* nested templates; we only want outermost raw  
    // So instead, slice directly between open+2 and j-2 for outermost:  
    const raw \= text.slice(open + 2, j \- 2).trim();  
  
    const call \= parseOneTemplate(raw, open, j);  
    if (call) calls.push(call);  
  
    i \= j;  
  }  
  
  return calls;  
}  
  
function parseOneTemplate(raw: string, start: number, end: number): TemplateCall | null {  
  // Split on '|' at depth 0 (avoid splitting inside nested templates or links)  
  const parts \= splitPipesAtTopLevel(raw);  
  if (parts.length \=== 0) return null;  
  
  const name \= parts\[0\].trim();  
  const args: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  const kwargs: Record<string, string\> \= {};  
  
  for (const p of parts.slice(1)) {  
    const s \= p.trim();  
    if (!s) continue;  
    const eq \= s.indexOf("=");  
    if (eq \> 0) {  
      const k \= s.slice(0, eq).trim();  
      const v \= s.slice(eq + 1).trim();  
      kwargs\[k\] \= v;  
    } else {  
      args.push(s);  
    }  
  }  
  
  return { name, args, kwargs, raw, start, end };  
}  
  
function splitPipesAtTopLevel(raw: string): string\[\] {  
  const out: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  let buf \= "";  
  let depthTpl \= 0;  
  let depthLink \= 0; // \[\[ \]\]  
  for (let i \= 0; i < raw.length; i++) {  
    const ch \= raw\[i\];  
    // detect nested template open/close  
    if (raw.startsWith("{{", i)) {  
      depthTpl++;  
      buf += "{{";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (raw.startsWith("}}", i)) {  
      depthTpl \= Math.max(0, depthTpl \- 1);  
      buf += "}}";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    // detect wikilinks  
    if (raw.startsWith("\[\[", i)) {  
      depthLink++;  
      buf += "\[\[";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (raw.startsWith("\]\]", i)) {  
      depthLink \= Math.max(0, depthLink \- 1);  
      buf += "\]\]";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
  
    if (ch \=== "|" && depthTpl \=== 0 && depthLink \=== 0) {  
      out.push(buf);  
      buf \= "";  
    } else {  
      buf += ch;  
    }  
  }  
  out.push(buf);  
  return out;  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Pronunciation extraction (simple)  
\============================================================================ \*/  
function extractPronunciation(text: string, lang: string): Pronunciation | undefined {  
  // Look for {{IPA|el|/.../}} or {{IPA|lang=el|/.../}} etc.  
  const calls \= parseTemplates(text);  
  const ipas: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const c of calls) {  
    if (normalizeTemplateName(c.name) !== "ipa") continue;  
  
    // heuristics  
    // Common patterns:  
    //  - {{IPA|el|/.../}}  
    //  - {{IPA|lang=el|/.../}}  
    const langArg \= c.args\[0\]?.trim();  
    const kwLang \= (c.kwargs\["lang"\] ?? c.kwargs\["1"\])?.trim();  
  
    const isLangOk \= (kwLang && kwLang \=== lang) || (langArg && langArg \=== lang);  
    if (!isLangOk) continue;  
  
    // IPA strings are usually subsequent args; collect anything that looks like /.../  
    for (const a of c.args.slice(1)) {  
      const t \= a.trim();  
      if (t.startsWith("/") && t.endsWith("/")) ipas.push(t);  
    }  
    // Sometimes IPA is provided via "1=/.../" etc; add if present  
    for (const \[k, v\] of Object.entries(c.kwargs)) {  
      const t \= v.trim();  
      if (t.startsWith("/") && t.endsWith("/")) ipas.push(t);  
      // ignore others  
    }  
  }  
  if (ipas.length \=== 0) return undefined;  
  return { IPA: ipas.length \=== 1 ? ipas\[0\] : ipas };  
}  
  
function normalizeTemplateName(name: string): string {  
  return name.trim().replace(/\_/g, " ").toLowerCase();  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Block decoding  
\============================================================================ \*/  
type DecodeBlockInput \= {  
  lang: string;  
  pageTitle: string;  
  edition: string;  
  posHeading: string;  
  blockText: string;  
  templates: TemplateCall\[\];  
  pronunciation?: Pronunciation;  
  includeRaw: boolean;  
};  
  
function decodeBlock(input: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // Decide if inflected vs lemma by presence of el-form-of-\* templates  
  // and/or headword templates.  
  const lang \= input.lang;  
  
  const decoders \= getDecodersForLang(lang);  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  
  // 1) Inflected-form decoders (highest priority)  
  for (const d of decoders.formOfDecoders) {  
    const entries \= d(input);  
    if (entries.length) out.push(...entries);  
  }  
  if (out.length) return out;  
  
  // 2) Lemma decoders  
  for (const d of decoders.lemmaDecoders) {  
    const entries \= d(input);  
    if (entries.length) out.push(...entries);  
  }  
  if (out.length) return out;  
  
  // 3) Fallback: unknown lexeme-ish  
  const fallback: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`${lang}:${input.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: input.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: mapPosHeadingToPos(input.posHeading),  
    pronunciation: input.pronunciation,  
  };  
  if (input.includeRaw) {  
    fallback.\_raw \= {  
      edition: input.edition,  
      pageTitle: input.pageTitle,  
      wikitextSlice: input.blockText.slice(0, 2000),  
      templates: input.templates,  
      posHeading: input.posHeading,  
    };  
  }  
  return \[fallback\];  
}  
  
function getDecodersForLang(lang: string): {  
  formOfDecoders: Array<(i: DecodeBlockInput) => StructuredEntry\[\]>;  
  lemmaDecoders: Array<(i: DecodeBlockInput) => StructuredEntry\[\]>;  
} {  
  if (lang \=== "el") {  
    return {  
      formOfDecoders: \[  
        decodeElFormOfVerb,  
        decodeElFormOfNoun,  
        decodeElFormOfAdj,  
        decodeElArticleForm, // "του" etc often appear as entries  
        decodeElPronounForm, // "μου" etc  
      \],  
      lemmaDecoders: \[  
        decodeElVerbLemma,  
        decodeElNounLemma,  
        decodeElAdjLemma,  
        decodeElAdvLemma,  
        decodeElArticleLemma,  
        decodeElPronounLemma,  
        decodeElParticipleLemma,  
      \],  
    };  
  }  
  // Generic fallback language (very minimal)  
  return {  
    formOfDecoders: \[\],  
    lemmaDecoders: \[\],  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Greek decoders (MVP heuristics)  
NOTE: These are robust to variability only to a point.  
You will iterate on these with real fixtures.  
\============================================================================ \*/  
  
function baseRaw(i: DecodeBlockInput) {  
  return i.includeRaw  
    ? {  
        edition: i.edition,  
        pageTitle: i.pageTitle,  
        wikitextSlice: i.blockText.slice(0, 4000),  
        templates: i.templates,  
        posHeading: i.posHeading,  
      }  
    : undefined;  
}  
  
function decodeElFormOfVerb(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of i.templates) {  
    if (normalizeTemplateName(t.name) !== "el-form-of-verb") continue;  
  
    const lemma \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim();  
    if (!lemma) continue;  
  
    const features \= decodeElVerbFeaturesFromTemplate(t);  
    const id \= \`el:${i.pageTitle}#verb.${verbFeatureKey(features)}\`;  
  
    const entry: InflectedEntry \= {  
      id,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: i.pageTitle,  
      part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
      pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
      hyphenation: undefined, // fill later if you implement hyphen templates  
      lemma: {  
        id: \`el:${lemma}\`,  
        form: lemma,  
        part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
      },  
      features,  
      morphology: undefined, // optional: your own morphology layer  
      usage: extractUsageExamplesBasic(i.blockText, "el"),  
    };  
    if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
    out.push(entry);  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeElVerbLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // Detect {{el-verb ...}} in block  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-verb");  
  if (!has) return out;  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    class: "verb.act.ω", // placeholder; you can infer later from template params  
    voice\_type: "active",  
    morphology: {}, // you’ll fill this later with your own morphology engine  
    paradigm: {}, // optionally from conj templates / later  
    translations: extractTranslationsBasic(i.blockText, "en"),  
    derivations: extractDerivedTermsBasic(i.blockText),  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  
  out.push(entry);  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeElFormOfNoun(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of i.templates) {  
    if (normalizeTemplateName(t.name) !== "el-form-of-noun") continue;  
  
    const lemma \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim();  
    if (!lemma) continue;  
  
    const features \= decodeElNominalFeaturesFromTemplate(t);  
    const id \= \`el:${i.pageTitle}#noun.${nominalFeatureKey(features)}\`;  
  
    const entry: InflectedEntry \= {  
      id,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: i.pageTitle,  
      part\_of\_speech: "noun",  
      pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
      lemma: { id: \`el:${lemma}\`, form: lemma, part\_of\_speech: "noun" },  
      features,  
      usage: extractUsageExamplesBasic(i.blockText, "el"),  
    };  
    if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
    out.push(entry);  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeElNounLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-noun");  
  if (!has) return \[\];  
  
  const gender \= inferGenderFromElNounTemplate(i.templates) ?? undefined;  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "noun",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    gender,  
    class: gender ? \`noun.${gender\[0\]}\` : undefined,  
    morphology: {},  
    paradigm: {}, // optional  
    translations: extractTranslationsBasic(i.blockText, "en"),  
    derivations: extractDerivedTermsBasic(i.blockText),  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
function decodeElFormOfAdj(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of i.templates) {  
    if (normalizeTemplateName(t.name) !== "el-form-of-adj") continue;  
  
    const lemma \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim();  
    if (!lemma) continue;  
  
    const features \= decodeElNominalFeaturesFromTemplate(t);  
    // adjective forms can have gender ambiguity; keep as-is  
    const id \= \`el:${i.pageTitle}#adj.${nominalFeatureKey(features)}\`;  
  
    const entry: InflectedEntry \= {  
      id,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: i.pageTitle,  
      part\_of\_speech: "adjective",  
      pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
      lemma: { id: \`el:${lemma}\`, form: lemma, part\_of\_speech: "adjective" },  
      features,  
      usage: extractUsageExamplesBasic(i.blockText, "el"),  
    };  
    if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
    out.push(entry);  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeElAdjLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-adj");  
  if (!has) return \[\];  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "adjective",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    class: "adj", // refine later  
    morphology: {},  
    paradigm: {},  
    translations: extractTranslationsBasic(i.blockText, "en"),  
    derivations: extractDerivedTermsBasic(i.blockText),  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
function decodeElAdvLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-adv");  
  if (!has) return \[\];  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "adverb",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    translations: extractTranslationsBasic(i.blockText, "en"),  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
function decodeElParticipleLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // There isn’t one universal template; MVP: if POS heading says "Participle" or template el-part exists  
  const isPartHeading \= mapPosHeadingToPos(i.posHeading) \=== "participle";  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-part");  
  if (!isPartHeading && !has) return \[\];  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "participle",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    morphology: {},  
    paradigm: {},  
    translations: extractTranslationsBasic(i.blockText, "en"),  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
/\* ---- Articles & pronouns (minimal) ------------------------------------ \*/  
  
function decodeElArticleLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // Some pages use templates like {{el-article}}; not guaranteed. MVP heuristic:  
  const isArticle \= mapPosHeadingToPos(i.posHeading) \=== "article";  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-article");  
  if (!isArticle && !has) return \[\];  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "article",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    paradigm: {}, // you’ll later populate by reading known table templates  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
function decodeElArticleForm(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // MVP: detect "article" POS + presence of "form of" templates is inconsistent.  
  // We'll treat the page as INFLECTED\_FORM if it contains an explicit “form of” template naming el article.  
  // Many projects encode as "form of ο" etc; you’ll refine with fixtures.  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of i.templates) {  
    const n \= normalizeTemplateName(t.name);  
    if (n !== "form of" && n !== "inflection of") continue;  
  
    const target \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim(); // often lemma link  
    if (!target) continue;  
  
    // Try to spot if target is the definite article "ο" / "η" / "το"  
    if (!\["ο", "η", "το"\].includes(stripWikiMarkup(target))) continue;  
  
    const features: Features \= {}; // fill later if args include case/gender/number  
    const entry: InflectedEntry \= {  
      id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}#art.form\`,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: i.pageTitle,  
      part\_of\_speech: "article",  
      pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
      lemma: { id: \`el:ο\`, form: "ο", part\_of\_speech: "article", subtype: "definite" },  
      features,  
    };  
    if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
    out.push(entry);  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeElPronounLemma(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  const isPron \= mapPosHeadingToPos(i.posHeading) \=== "pronoun";  
  const has \= i.templates.some((t) => normalizeTemplateName(t.name) \=== "el-pron");  
  if (!isPron && !has) return \[\];  
  
  const entry: LexemeEntry \= {  
    id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: i.pageTitle,  
    part\_of\_speech: "pronoun",  
    pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
    paradigm: {},  
  };  
  if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
  return \[entry\];  
}  
  
function decodeElPronounForm(i: DecodeBlockInput): StructuredEntry\[\] {  
  // MVP: recognize some “form-of” templates for pronouns if present.  
  const out: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of i.templates) {  
    const n \= normalizeTemplateName(t.name);  
    if (n !== "form of" && n !== "inflection of") continue;  
  
    const lemma \= stripWikiMarkup((t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim());  
    if (!lemma) continue;  
  
    const isLikelyPronounLemma \= \["εγώ", "εσύ", "αυτός", "αυτή", "αυτό", "εμείς", "εσείς", "αυτοί"\].includes(lemma);  
    if (!isLikelyPronounLemma) continue;  
  
    const entry: InflectedEntry \= {  
      id: \`el:${i.pageTitle}#pron.form\`,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: i.pageTitle,  
      part\_of\_speech: "pronoun",  
      pronunciation: i.pronunciation,  
      lemma: { id: \`el:${lemma}\`, form: lemma, part\_of\_speech: "pronoun" },  
      features: { clitic: true }, // often true; you’ll refine  
    };  
    if (i.includeRaw) entry.\_raw \= baseRaw(i);  
    out.push(entry);  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Feature decoding helpers  
\============================================================================ \*/  
  
function decodeElVerbFeaturesFromTemplate(t: TemplateCall): Features {  
  // We expect a variety of param styles. MVP supports common ones:  
  // - pers=3s, 3sg, etc  
  // - tense=aorist / aor / past  
  // - mood=ind / indicative  
  // - voice=act / active  
  const f: Features \= {};  
  
  // positional args sometimes include short codes; keywords are more reliable  
  const pers \= (t.kwargs\["pers"\] ?? t.kwargs\["person"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (pers) {  
    const m \= /^(\[123\])\\s\*(\[sp\]g|s|p)?/i.exec(pers.replace(/\\s+/g, ""));  
    if (m) {  
      f.person \= Number(m\[1\]) as 1 | 2 | 3;  
      if (m\[2\]) f.number \= m\[2\].toLowerCase().includes("p") ? "plural" : "singular";  
    }  
  }  
  
  const tenseRaw \= (t.kwargs\["tense"\] ?? t.kwargs\["t"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (tenseRaw) f.tense \= normalizeTense(tenseRaw);  
  
  const moodRaw \= (t.kwargs\["mood"\] ?? t.kwargs\["m"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (moodRaw) f.mood \= normalizeMood(moodRaw);  
  
  const voiceRaw \= (t.kwargs\["voice"\] ?? t.kwargs\["v"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (voiceRaw) f.voice \= normalizeVoice(voiceRaw);  
  
  // Some templates might encode 3rd/sg etc in positional args; attempt fallback scan:  
  if (!f.person || !f.number || !f.tense || !f.mood || !f.voice) {  
    const bag \= \[...t.args, ...Object.values(t.kwargs)\].join(" ").toLowerCase();  
  
    if (!f.person) {  
      if (/\\b1\\b/.test(bag)) f.person \= 1;  
      else if (/\\b2\\b/.test(bag)) f.person \= 2;  
      else if (/\\b3\\b/.test(bag)) f.person \= 3;  
    }  
    if (!f.number) {  
      if (/\\bpl\\b|\\bplural\\b/.test(bag)) f.number \= "plural";  
      else if (/\\bsg\\b|\\bsingular\\b/.test(bag)) f.number \= "singular";  
    }  
    if (!f.tense) {  
      if (/\\baor/.test(bag)) f.tense \= "aorist";  
      else if (/\\bimpf|\\bimperfect/.test(bag)) f.tense \= "imperfect";  
      else if (/\\bpres|\\bpresent/.test(bag)) f.tense \= "present";  
      else if (/\\bfut|\\bfuture/.test(bag)) f.tense \= "future";  
    }  
    if (!f.mood) {  
      if (/\\bind\\b|\\bindicative/.test(bag)) f.mood \= "indicative";  
      else if (/\\bsubj|\\bsubjunctive/.test(bag)) f.mood \= "subjunctive";  
      else if (/\\bimp\\b|\\bimperative/.test(bag)) f.mood \= "imperative";  
    }  
    if (!f.voice) {  
      if (/\\bact\\b|\\bactive/.test(bag)) f.voice \= "active";  
      else if (/\\bmid\\b|\\bmiddle/.test(bag)) f.voice \= "middle";  
      else if (/\\bpass\\b|\\bpassive/.test(bag)) f.voice \= "passive";  
    }  
  }  
  
  return f;  
}  
  
function decodeElNominalFeaturesFromTemplate(t: TemplateCall): Features {  
  // MVP supports keys like case=gen, number=sg, gender=m etc.  
  const f: Features \= {};  
  
  const caseRaw \= (t.kwargs\["case"\] ?? t.kwargs\["c"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (caseRaw) f.case \= normalizeCase(caseRaw);  
  
  const numRaw \= (t.kwargs\["number"\] ?? t.kwargs\["n"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (numRaw) f.number \= normalizeNumber(numRaw);  
  
  const gRaw \= (t.kwargs\["gender"\] ?? t.kwargs\["g"\] ?? "").trim();  
  if (gRaw) f.gender \= normalizeGender(gRaw);  
  
  // fallback: scan bag  
  const bag \= \[...t.args, ...Object.values(t.kwargs)\].join(" ").toLowerCase();  
  if (!f.case) {  
    if (/\\bgen\\b|\\bgenitive\\b/.test(bag)) f.case \= "genitive";  
    else if (/\\bnom\\b|\\bnominative\\b/.test(bag)) f.case \= "nominative";  
    else if (/\\bacc\\b|\\baccusative\\b/.test(bag)) f.case \= "accusative";  
    else if (/\\bvoc\\b|\\bvocative\\b/.test(bag)) f.case \= "vocative";  
  }  
  if (!f.number) {  
    if (/\\bpl\\b|\\bplural\\b/.test(bag)) f.number \= "plural";  
    else if (/\\bsg\\b|\\bsingular\\b/.test(bag)) f.number \= "singular";  
  }  
  if (!f.gender) {  
    if (/\\bm\\b|\\bmasc/.test(bag)) f.gender \= "masculine";  
    else if (/\\bf\\b|\\bfem/.test(bag)) f.gender \= "feminine";  
    else if (/\\bn\\b|\\bneut/.test(bag)) f.gender \= "neuter";  
  }  
  
  return f;  
}  
  
function normalizeTense(x: string): VerbTense {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase();  
  if (s.startsWith("aor")) return "aorist";  
  if (s.startsWith("pres")) return "present";  
  if (s.startsWith("impf") || s.startsWith("imperfect")) return "imperfect";  
  if (s.startsWith("fut")) return "future";  
  if (s \=== "past") return "aorist"; // pragmatic mapping for Greek; refine if needed  
  return x;  
}  
  
function normalizeMood(x: string): VerbMood {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase();  
  if (s.startsWith("ind")) return "indicative";  
  if (s.startsWith("subj")) return "subjunctive";  
  if (s.startsWith("imp")) return "imperative";  
  return x;  
}  
  
function normalizeVoice(x: string): VerbVoice {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase();  
  if (s.startsWith("act")) return "active";  
  if (s.startsWith("mid")) return "middle";  
  if (s.startsWith("pass")) return "passive";  
  return x;  
}  
  
function normalizeCase(x: string): GrCase | undefined {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase();  
  if (s.startsWith("nom")) return "nominative";  
  if (s.startsWith("gen")) return "genitive";  
  if (s.startsWith("acc")) return "accusative";  
  if (s.startsWith("voc")) return "vocative";  
  return undefined;  
}  
  
function normalizeNumber(x: string): GrNumber | undefined {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase();  
  if (s.startsWith("sg") || s.startsWith("sing")) return "singular";  
  if (s.startsWith("pl") || s.startsWith("plur")) return "plural";  
  return undefined;  
}  
  
function normalizeGender(x: string): Gender | Gender\[\] | undefined {  
  const s \= x.toLowerCase().replace(/\\s+/g, "");  
  // allow "m|n" or "m,n"  
  const parts \= s.split(/\[|,\]/).filter(Boolean);  
  const mapOne \= (p: string): Gender | undefined => {  
    if (p.startsWith("m")) return "masculine";  
    if (p.startsWith("f")) return "feminine";  
    if (p.startsWith("n")) return "neuter";  
    return undefined;  
  };  
  const gs \= parts.map(mapOne).filter(Boolean) as Gender\[\];  
  if (gs.length \=== 0) {  
    const one \= mapOne(s);  
    return one;  
  }  
  return gs.length \=== 1 ? gs\[0\] : gs;  
}  
  
function verbFeatureKey(f: Features): string {  
  const tense \= f.tense ?? "unk";  
  const mood \= f.mood ?? "unk";  
  const voice \= f.voice ?? "unk";  
  const person \= f.person ?? "x";  
  const num \= f.number \=== "singular" ? "sg" : f.number \=== "plural" ? "pl" : "x";  
  return \`${tense}.${mood}.${voice}.${person}${num}\`;  
}  
  
function nominalFeatureKey(f: Features): string {  
  const c \= f.case ?? "unk";  
  const n \= f.number \=== "singular" ? "sg" : f.number \=== "plural" ? "pl" : "x";  
  const g \=  
    Array.isArray(f.gender) ? f.gender.map((x) => x\[0\]).join("") :  
    typeof f.gender \=== "string" ? f.gender\[0\] :  
    "x";  
  return \`${c}.${n}.${g}\`;  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Basic content extraction (MVP): examples, translations, derived terms  
These are intentionally conservative (low risk of hallucinated structure).  
You will iterate on these with real wikitext fixtures.  
\============================================================================ \*/  
  
function extractUsageExamplesBasic(blockText: string, lang: string): Array<Record<string, string\>> | undefined {  
  // Very conservative: look for lines starting with "#:" (example) and optionally a translation line.  
  // This is not consistent across entries; treat as optional.  
  const lines \= blockText.split("\\n");  
  const out: Array<Record<string, string\>> \= \[\];  
  for (const ln of lines) {  
    const s \= ln.trim();  
    if (!s.startsWith("#:")) continue;  
    const ex \= s.replace(/^#:\\s\*/, "").trim();  
    if (!ex) continue;  
    // Try to strip wiki markup from the example  
    out.push({ \[lang\]: stripWikiMarkup(ex) });  
  }  
  return out.length ? out : undefined;  
}  
  
function extractTranslationsBasic(blockText: string, targetLang: string): Record<string, Array<{ gloss: string }>> | undefined {  
  // Translations are messy. MVP:  
  // - find a "====Translations====" section  
  // - within it, collect bullet lines that include targetLang code like "\* en: ..."  
  const lines \= blockText.split("\\n");  
  const out: Record<string, Array<{ gloss: string }>> \= {};  
  let inTranslations \= false;  
  
  for (const ln of lines) {  
    const s \= ln.trim();  
    if (/^====\\s\*Translations\\s\*====\\s\*$/.test(s)) {  
      inTranslations \= true;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (inTranslations && /^====\[^=\]/.test(s)) {  
      // next top-level subsection  
      inTranslations \= false;  
    }  
    if (!inTranslations) continue;  
  
    // Patterns vary. Handle simple ones:  
    // \* en: {{t|en|write}} ...  
    // \* English: write; record ...  
    if (s.startsWith("\*")) {  
      const lower \= s.toLowerCase();  
      if (lower.includes(\`${targetLang}:\`) || lower.includes("english:")) {  
        const gloss \= stripWikiMarkup(s.replace(/^\\\*\\s\*/,""));  
        if (!out\[targetLang\]) out\[targetLang\] \= \[\];  
        out\[targetLang\].push({ gloss });  
      }  
    }  
  }  
  
  return Object.keys(out).length ? out : undefined;  
}  
  
function extractDerivedTermsBasic(blockText: string): string\[\] | undefined {  
  // Find "====Derived terms====" or "====Derived terms====" and grab bullet items.  
  const lines \= blockText.split("\\n");  
  let inDerived \= false;  
  const out: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const ln of lines) {  
    const s \= ln.trim();  
    if (/^====\\s\*Derived terms\\s\*====\\s\*$/.test(s)) {  
      inDerived \= true;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (inDerived && /^====\[^=\]/.test(s)) inDerived \= false;  
    if (!inDerived) continue;  
  
    if (s.startsWith("\*")) {  
      const item \= stripWikiMarkup(s.replace(/^\\\*\\s\*/, ""));  
      // crude: take first token if it's a link or word  
      if (item) out.push(item);  
    }  
  }  
  return out.length ? dedupe(out) : undefined;  
}  
  
function dedupe(xs: string\[\]): string\[\] {  
  return \[...new Set(xs.map((x) => x.trim()).filter(Boolean))\];  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Lemma expansion  
\============================================================================ \*/  
async function expandLemmaForInflected(  
  candidates: StructuredEntry\[\],  
  options: FetchWiktionaryOptions,  
  warnings: string\[\]  
): Promise<void\> {  
  const inflected \= candidates.filter((c): c is InflectedEntry => c.type \=== "INFLECTED\_FORM");  
  if (inflected.length \=== 0) return;  
  
  // Fetch each unique lemma once  
  const lemmaForms \= dedupe(inflected.map((x) => x.lemma.form));  
  const lemmaMap \= new Map<string, LexemeEntry | null\>();  
  
  for (const lemma of lemmaForms) {  
    const r \= await fetchWiktionary(lemma, { ...options, expandLemma: false }).catch((e) => {  
      warnings.push(\`Failed to expand lemma "${lemma}": ${String(e)}\`);  
      return null;  
    });  
    const lex \= r?.candidates.find((c): c is LexemeEntry => c.type \=== "LEXEME") ?? null;  
    lemmaMap.set(lemma, lex);  
  }  
  
  for (const infl of inflected) {  
    const lex \= lemmaMap.get(infl.lemma.form);  
    if (!lex) continue;  
    // Attach a few helpful fields without duplicating the whole lexeme  
    infl.lemma.id \= lex.id;  
    infl.lemma.part\_of\_speech \= lex.part\_of\_speech;  
    infl.lemma.class \= lex.class;  
    if (lex.part\_of\_speech \=== "noun" && (lex as any).gender) infl.lemma.gender \= (lex as any).gender;  
  }  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Small utilities  
\============================================================================ \*/  
function escapeRegex(s: string): string {  
  return s.replace(/\[.\*+?^${}()|\[\\\]\\\\\]/g, "\\\\$&");  
}  
  
function stripWikiMarkup(s: string): string {  
  // minimal cleanup: remove \[\[...\]\] keeping display text, remove italics/bold markup  
  let out \= s;  
  
  // \[\[target|label\]\] -> label; \[\[target\]\] -> target  
  out \= out.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^|\\\]\]+)\\|(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$2");  
  out \= out.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$1");  
  
  // ''italics'' and '''bold'''  
  out \= out.replace(/'''''/g, "");  
  out \= out.replace(/'''/g, "");  
  out \= out.replace(/''/g, "");  
  
  // templates still present -> keep as-is for now or strip crudely  
  out \= out.replace(/\\{\\{\[^}\]+\\}\\}/g, "");  
  
  return out.replace(/\\s+/g, " ").trim();  
}  
  
function inferGenderFromElNounTemplate(templates: TemplateCall\[\]): Gender | null {  
  // el-noun template often includes gender markers; we do a simple scan.  
  for (const t of templates) {  
    if (normalizeTemplateName(t.name) !== "el-noun") continue;  
    const bag \= \[...t.args, ...Object.values(t.kwargs)\].join(" ").toLowerCase();  
    if (/\\b(m|masc|masculine)\\b/.test(bag)) return "masculine";  
    if (/\\b(f|fem|feminine)\\b/.test(bag)) return "feminine";  
    if (/\\b(n|neut|neuter)\\b/.test(bag)) return "neuter";  
  }  
  return null;  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================================  
Example usage (remove from library file if you want)  
\============================================================================ \*/  
/\*  
(async () => {  
  const r1 = await fetchWiktionary("έγραψε", { lang: "el", pos: "verb", includeRaw: true, expandLemma: true });  
  console.log(JSON.stringify(r1, null, 2));  
  
  const r2 = await fetchWiktionary("σπίτι", { lang: "el", pos: "noun" });  
  console.log(JSON.stringify(r2, null, 2));  
})();  
\*/
```

## What you now have (today)

-   A working, extensible `fetchWiktionary(queryTerm, options)` that:
    
    -   calls **MediaWiki Action API** (`action=parse`) on **en.wiktionary**
        
    -   slices out the **Greek** language block (`==Greek==`)
        
    -   splits into POS blocks (`===Verb===`, `===Noun===`, …)
        
    -   parses template calls (`{{...}}`) with nesting safety
        
    -   decodes the minimal Greek template set into your **LEXEME / INFLECTED\_FORM** structures
        
    -   optionally expands lemma info for inflected forms (`expandLemma: true`)
        
    -   returns multiple candidates (homonymy / multi-POS)

This MVP uses conservative heuristics. Next steps that will quickly boost accuracy:

1.  **Real fixtures**: store wikitext snapshots for ~50 Greek words and write tests.
    
2.  Implement robust decoders for:
    
    -   hyphenation templates (Greek-specific)
        
    -   conjugation/declension tables (optional; you can postpone)
        
3.  Improve function words:
    
    -   use the actual Greek templates used on en.wiktionary for articles/pronouns
        
4.  Improve translations extraction:
    
    -   parse `{{t|en|...}}` templates properly into glosses

Yes — and we can now be very concrete, because **the raw wikitext for the Greek section of *έγραψε* and *γράφω* is directly retrievable** (as HTML “view source”, or as JSON via the Action API).

## 1) “Raw template block” for **έγραψε** (Greek section)

On English Wiktionary, the **Greek section wikitext** for **έγραψε** is literally:

```
wikitext

\===Verb===  
{{head|el|verbf}}  
\# {{infl of|el|γράφω||3s|spast}}
```

That comes from the “view source” (section edit) page. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5)

So: for non-lemma verb forms like **έγραψε**, your parser can often start from `{{infl of|...}}` and treat it as a *structured inflection pointer to the lemma*.

## 2) “Raw template block” for **γράφω** (Greek section)

The Greek verb section for **γράφω** contains (among other things) these key templates:

-   headword + principal parts:
    
    -   `{{el-verb|past=έγραψα|passive=γράφομαι}}`
        
-   example sentence:
    
    -   `{{ux|el|...|t=...}}`
        
-   conjugation table template with lots of parameters:
    
    -   `{{el-conjug-1st |augmented=1 |present=γράφ |a-imperfect=έγραφ |a-dependent=γράψ |a-simplepast=έγραψ |...}}`
        
-   link + gloss templates all over:
    
    -   `{{l|el|αντιγράφω|gloss=to copy, to cheat}}`
        
-   qualifiers:
    
    -   `{{q|for traffic violation, etc}}`
        

All of that is visible in the section “view source” for the Greek verb section. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)

---

## 3) About your endpoint confusion (and why your tests behaved that way)

### Why `el.wiktionary.org/.../page/...` said “page does not exist”

Because **the page exists on *English* Wiktionary**, not necessarily on **Greek-language Wiktionary**.

You already observed:

-   `https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/έγραψε` exists (HTML page)
    
-   `https://el.wiktionary.org/w/rest.php/v1/page/έγραψε` returns JSON but says “does not exist”
    

That’s not an API failure — it’s just **a different wiki with different page inventory**.

### Why `.../api/rest_v1/page/summary/...` said “Domain not allowed”

The Wikimedia “REST v1” stack has allowlisting / routing constraints in some deployments; in practice, for Wiktionary you’ll have a much easier time using either:

-   the **MediaWiki Action API** (`/w/api.php`) for wikitext, or
    
-   the **MediaWiki REST API** (`/w/rest.php`) for page objects/content routes
    

(MediaWiki documents both REST and Action APIs separately.) [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AREST_API?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## 4) The pragmatic plan for `fetchWiktionary(query_term)` in TypeScript

You want **structured YAML/JSON** like your schemas, across lemma + non-lemma forms. The cleanest approach is:

### Phase A — Fetch the raw source deterministically (don’t scrape the pretty HTML)

Prefer the **Action API** to fetch wikitext (stable, explicit, meant for this):

**Option A1: `action=query&prop=revisions` (recommended)**

-   Gives you the page wikitext without needing “edit pages”.
    
-   MediaWiki explicitly documents this as the way to “get the contents of a page”. [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AGet_the_contents_of_a_page?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    

**Option A2: `action=parse&prop=wikitext`**

-   Also works, but revisions is the canonical “get me source” path.
    

**Fallback (only if needed):** `?action=edit&section=...` “view source” like we used above (works even when blocked from editing, and still shows the text), but it’s an HTML wrapper around the same wikitext.

### Phase B — Decide which Wiktionary to query (project selection)

Given `lang:"el"`:

1.  Try `https://el.wiktionary.org/...` (Greek Wiktionary)
    
2.  If missing, fallback to `https://en.wiktionary.org/...` and extract the `==Greek==` section.
    

This matches reality: many Greek forms are richly described on **enwiktionary** even when absent on **elwiktionary**.

### Phase C — Parse wikitext into your schema (template-driven extraction)

You do **not** need a “zicky-tech full parser” to get far.

For Greek, 80/20 comes from a small set of templates, because Wiktionary entries are heavily template-encoded.

#### Minimum “must support” templates for Greek (starter set)

This will cover a huge fraction of verb-form and common headword cases you care about:

**Core structure**

-   Language / POS headings: `==Greek==`, `===Verb===`, `===Noun===`, etc.
    
-   Headword templates:
    
    -   `{{head|el|...}}` (common for forms) [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5)
        
    -   `{{el-verb|...}}` (lemmas) [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)
        
    -   (later) `{{el-noun|...}}`, `{{el-adj|...}}`, etc.
        

**Inflection pointer (critical for non-lemma forms)**

-   `{{infl of|el|LEMMA|...}}` [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5)  
    This is where you get:
    
-   lemma
    
-   person/number/tense-ish codes (like `3s`, `spast`)
    

**Examples**

-   `{{ux|el|...|t=...}}` [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)
    

**Conjugation / paradigms**

-   `{{el-conjug-1st|...}}` [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)  
    This is your main source for stems (present, aorist, passive stems), augment flags, and “principal parts”-like fields.
    

**Linking/gloss micro-templates**

-   `{{l|el|...}}`
    
-   `{{q|...}}` [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)
    

That’s enough to build your **LEXEME** and **INFLECTED\_FORM** objects for verbs in a very robust way.

### Phase D — Produce your normalized output objects

Implement a mapper layer:

-   **If page has `{{infl of|el|...}}` in the Greek section**:
    
    -   emit `type: INFLECTED_FORM`
        
    -   set `lemma` from template arg 2
        
    -   map short codes (`3s`, `spast`, etc.) through a lookup table to your ontology
        
    -   optionally call `fetchWiktionary(lemma)` to enrich with lexeme paradigm data
        
-   **If page has `{{el-verb|...}}` in Greek section**:
    
    -   emit `type: LEXEME`
        
    -   parse `past=...`, `passive=...`
        
    -   parse `el-conjug-1st` params into stems + paradigm slots
        

### Phase E — API ergonomics (your requested signature)

Proposed signature:

```
TypeScript

type FetchWiktionaryOptions \= {  
  lang?: string;          // e.g. "el"  
  pos?: string;           // e.g. "verb"  
  projectHint?: "elwiktionary" | "enwiktionary";  
  includeLemma?: boolean; // if query is inflected, also fetch lemma and attach  
};  
  
async function fetchWiktionary(queryTerm: string, opts: FetchWiktionaryOptions \= {}): Promise<WiktionaryEntry\>;
```
