```
TypeScript

/\*\*  
 \* Wiktionary (MediaWiki) extractor — TypeScript MVP  
 \* -------------------------------------------------  
 \* What this implements (now):  
 \*  1) HTTP fetch via MediaWiki Action API (action=parse)  
 \*  2) WikiText section extraction (language + POS blocks)  
 \*  3) Minimal brace-template parser for {{...}} with nesting support  
 \*  4) First Greek verb mappers:  
 \*      - INFLECTED\_FORM via {{infl of|el|LEMMA||3s|spast}} (common on en.wiktionary)  
 \*      - LEXEME via {{el-verb|...}} + (optional) {{el-conjug-1st|...}}  
 \*      - IPA via {{IPA|el|/.../}}  
 \*  
 \* What this deliberately does NOT do yet:  
 \*  - Robust translations extraction  
 \*  - Robust derived terms extraction  
 \*  - Full declension/conjugation table materialization  
 \*  
 \* Assumptions:  
 \*  - For Modern Greek coverage, prefer en.wiktionary.org and extract ==Greek== section.  
 \*  - No scraping of /wiki HTML pages.  
 \*/  
  
export type WiktionaryEdition \= "en" | "el" | "auto";  
export type EntryType \= "LEXEME" | "INFLECTED\_FORM" | "PHRASE";  
export type Pos \=  
  | "verb"  
  | "noun"  
  | "adjective"  
  | "participle"  
  | "adverb"  
  | "article"  
  | "pronoun"  
  | "unknown";  
  
export type GrNumber \= "singular" | "plural";  
export type VerbTense \= "present" | "aorist" | "imperfect" | "future" | string;  
export type VerbMood \= "indicative" | "subjunctive" | "imperative" | string;  
export type VerbVoice \= "active" | "middle" | "passive" | string;  
  
export interface Features {  
  person?: 1 | 2 | 3;  
  number?: GrNumber;  
  tense?: VerbTense;  
  mood?: VerbMood;  
  voice?: VerbVoice;  
  
  // (later) shared nominal features:  
  case?: "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative";  
  gender?: "masculine" | "feminine" | "neuter" | Array<"masculine" | "feminine" | "neuter"\>;  
  
  \[k: string\]: unknown;  
}  
  
export interface Pronunciation {  
  IPA?: string | string\[\];  
}  
  
export interface LemmaRef {  
  id?: string;  
  form: string;  
  part\_of\_speech?: Pos;  
  class?: string;  
}  
  
export interface BaseEntry {  
  id: string;  
  language: string; // e.g. "el"  
  type: EntryType;  
  form: string;  
  
  part\_of\_speech?: Pos;  
  pronunciation?: Pronunciation;  
  hyphenation?: string;  
  
  \_raw?: {  
    edition: string;  
    domain: string;  
    pageTitle: string;  
    langHeading?: string;  
    posHeading?: string;  
    wikitextSlice?: string;  
    templates?: TemplateCall\[\];  
  };  
}  
  
export interface LexemeEntry extends BaseEntry {  
  type: "LEXEME";  
  class?: string;  
  voice\_type?: string;  
  
  morphology?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  paradigm?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  
  translations?: Record<string, Array<{ gloss: string }>>;  
  derivations?: string\[\];  
}  
  
export interface InflectedEntry extends BaseEntry {  
  type: "INFLECTED\_FORM";  
  lemma: LemmaRef;  
  features: Features;  
  morphology?: Record<string, unknown\>;  
  usage?: Array<Record<string, string\>>;  
}  
  
export type StructuredEntry \= LexemeEntry | InflectedEntry;  
  
export interface FetchWiktionaryOptions {  
  lang?: string;                  // default "el"  
  pos?: Pos;                      // disambiguation hint  
  edition?: WiktionaryEdition;    // default "auto" (=> "en" for Greek)  
  prefer?: "wikitext";            // (future) html  
  includeRaw?: boolean;  
  timeoutMs?: number;             // default 15s  
}  
  
export interface FetchWiktionaryResult {  
  query: { input: string; lang?: string; pos?: Pos };  
  candidates: StructuredEntry\[\];  
  warnings: string\[\];  
  source: {  
    edition: "en" | "el";  
    domain: string;  
    pageTitle: string;  
    revisionId?: number;  
    fetchedAt: string;  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* MediaWiki Action API: action=parse  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
type MWParseResponse \= {  
  parse?: {  
    title: string;  
    pageid: number;  
    revid?: number;  
    wikitext?: string | { "\*": string };  
  };  
  error?: { code: string; info: string };  
};  
  
async function fetchParseWikitext(  
  domain: string,  
  pageTitle: string,  
  timeoutMs: number  
): Promise<MWParseResponse\> {  
  const url \=  
    \`https://${domain}/w/api.php\` +  
    \`?action=parse\` +  
    \`&page=${encodeURIComponent(pageTitle)}\` +  
    \`&prop=wikitext\` +  
    \`&format=json\` +  
    \`&formatversion=2\` +  
    \`&origin=\*\`;  
  
  const res \= await fetchWithTimeout(url, timeoutMs);  
  if (!res.ok) {  
    return { error: { code: "http\_error", info: \`HTTP ${res.status} ${res.statusText}\` } };  
  }  
  return (await res.json()) as MWParseResponse;  
}  
  
async function fetchWithTimeout(url: string, timeoutMs: number): Promise<Response\> {  
  const controller \= new AbortController();  
  const t \= setTimeout(() => controller.abort(), timeoutMs);  
  try {  
    return await fetch(url, { signal: controller.signal });  
  } finally {  
    clearTimeout(t);  
  }  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* WikiText section extraction  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
export interface WikiSection {  
  heading: string;      // e.g. "Greek", "Verb"  
  level: number;        // 2 for ==...==, 3 for ===...===, etc.  
  start: number;        // index in full text  
  end: number;          // index in full text  
  text: string;         // slice covering this section (heading included)  
}  
  
function extractSectionByHeading(  
  wikitext: string,  
  level: number,  
  heading: string  
): WikiSection | null {  
  // heading line: ==Greek== (level 2), ===Verb=== (level 3), etc.  
  const eq \= "=".repeat(level);  
  const re \= new RegExp(\`^${escapeRegex(eq)}\\\\s\*${escapeRegex(heading)}\\\\s\*${escapeRegex(eq)}\\\\s\*$\`, "m");  
  const m \= re.exec(wikitext);  
  if (!m) return null;  
  
  const start \= m.index;  
  const after \= wikitext.slice(start + m\[0\].length);  
  
  // Next section of same or higher level: e.g. for level 2, stop at next ^==...==.  
  // For level 3 inside a language section, stop at next ^===...=== OR next ^==...==.  
  const reNextSame \= new RegExp(\`^${escapeRegex(eq)}\[^=\].\*${escapeRegex(eq)}\\\\s\*$\`, "m");  
  const reNextHigher \= new RegExp(\`^==\[^=\].\*==\\\\s\*$\`, "m"); // level 2 as “higher” boundary  
  
  let nextIdx \= \-1;  
  
  const nextSame \= reNextSame.exec(after);  
  if (nextSame) nextIdx \= nextSame.index;  
  
  if (level \> 2) {  
    const nextHigher \= reNextHigher.exec(after);  
    if (nextHigher) {  
      if (nextIdx \=== \-1) nextIdx \= nextHigher.index;  
      else nextIdx \= Math.min(nextIdx, nextHigher.index);  
    }  
  }  
  
  const end \= nextIdx \=== \-1 ? wikitext.length : start + m\[0\].length + nextIdx;  
  return {  
    heading,  
    level,  
    start,  
    end,  
    text: wikitext.slice(start, end),  
  };  
}  
  
function splitSubsections(  
  sectionText: string,  
  level: number  
): Array<{ heading: string; level: number; text: string }> {  
  const eq \= "=".repeat(level);  
  const headingRe \= new RegExp(\`^${escapeRegex(eq)}\\\\s\*(\[^=\].\*?)\\\\s\*${escapeRegex(eq)}\\\\s\*$\`, "m");  
  
  const matches: Array<{ heading: string; idx: number; lineLen: number }> \= \[\];  
  const lines \= sectionText.split("\\n");  
  
  // We need indices in the original string, so we accumulate offset.  
  let offset \= 0;  
  for (const line of lines) {  
    const m \= headingRe.exec(line);  
    if (m) {  
      matches.push({ heading: m\[1\].trim(), idx: offset, lineLen: line.length });  
    }  
    offset += line.length + 1; // + newline  
  }  
  
  if (matches.length \=== 0) return \[\];  
  
  const out: Array<{ heading: string; level: number; text: string }> \= \[\];  
  for (let i \= 0; i < matches.length; i++) {  
    const cur \= matches\[i\];  
    const next \= matches\[i + 1\];  
    const start \= cur.idx;  
    const end \= next ? next.idx : sectionText.length;  
    out.push({ heading: cur.heading, level, text: sectionText.slice(start, end) });  
  }  
  return out;  
}  
  
function escapeRegex(s: string): string {  
  return s.replace(/\[.\*+?^${}()|\[\\\]\\\\\]/g, "\\\\$&");  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* Minimal template parser for {{...}} with nesting + pipe-splitting  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
export interface TemplateCall {  
  name: string;  
  args: string\[\];                 // positional  
  kwargs: Record<string, string\>; // key=value  
  raw: string;                    // inside braces  
  start: number;  
  end: number;  
}  
  
export function parseTemplates(wikitext: string): TemplateCall\[\] {  
  const out: TemplateCall\[\] \= \[\];  
  let i \= 0;  
  
  while (i < wikitext.length) {  
    const open \= wikitext.indexOf("{{", i);  
    if (open \=== \-1) break;  
  
    let depth \= 0;  
    let j \= open;  
  
    while (j < wikitext.length) {  
      if (wikitext.startsWith("{{", j)) {  
        depth++;  
        j += 2;  
        continue;  
      }  
      if (wikitext.startsWith("}}", j)) {  
        depth\--;  
        j += 2;  
        if (depth \=== 0) break;  
        continue;  
      }  
      j++;  
    }  
  
    if (depth !== 0) break; // unbalanced  
  
    const raw \= wikitext.slice(open + 2, j \- 2).trim();  
    const call \= parseOneTemplate(raw, open, j);  
    if (call) out.push(call);  
  
    i \= j;  
  }  
  
  return out;  
}  
  
function parseOneTemplate(raw: string, start: number, end: number): TemplateCall | null {  
  const parts \= splitPipesAtTopLevel(raw);  
  if (parts.length \=== 0) return null;  
  
  const name \= parts\[0\].trim();  
  const args: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  const kwargs: Record<string, string\> \= {};  
  
  for (const p of parts.slice(1)) {  
    const s \= p.trim();  
    if (!s) {  
      args.push(""); // preserve empties; Wiktionary uses empty positional args intentionally  
      continue;  
    }  
    const eq \= s.indexOf("=");  
    if (eq \> 0) {  
      const k \= s.slice(0, eq).trim();  
      const v \= s.slice(eq + 1).trim();  
      kwargs\[k\] \= v;  
    } else {  
      args.push(s);  
    }  
  }  
  
  return { name, args, kwargs, raw, start, end };  
}  
  
function splitPipesAtTopLevel(raw: string): string\[\] {  
  const out: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  let buf \= "";  
  
  let tplDepth \= 0;  // {{ }}  
  let linkDepth \= 0; // \[\[ \]\]  
  
  for (let i \= 0; i < raw.length; i++) {  
    if (raw.startsWith("{{", i)) {  
      tplDepth++;  
      buf += "{{";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (raw.startsWith("}}", i)) {  
      tplDepth \= Math.max(0, tplDepth \- 1);  
      buf += "}}";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (raw.startsWith("\[\[", i)) {  
      linkDepth++;  
      buf += "\[\[";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (raw.startsWith("\]\]", i)) {  
      linkDepth \= Math.max(0, linkDepth \- 1);  
      buf += "\]\]";  
      i++;  
      continue;  
    }  
  
    const ch \= raw\[i\];  
    if (ch \=== "|" && tplDepth \=== 0 && linkDepth \=== 0) {  
      out.push(buf);  
      buf \= "";  
    } else {  
      buf += ch;  
    }  
  }  
  
  out.push(buf);  
  return out;  
}  
  
function normTplName(s: string): string {  
  return s.trim().replace(/\_/g, " ").toLowerCase();  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* Greek-specific extractors (MVP)  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
function extractIPA(templates: TemplateCall\[\], langCode: string): Pronunciation | undefined {  
  const ipas: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const t of templates) {  
    if (normTplName(t.name) !== "ipa") continue;  
  
    // common patterns:  
    //  {{IPA|el|/ˈɣra.fo/}}  
    //  {{IPA|lang=el|/ˈɣra.fo/}}  
    const arg0 \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim();  
    const kwLang \= (t.kwargs\["lang"\] ?? "").trim();  
    const ok \= (arg0 \=== langCode) || (kwLang \=== langCode);  
    if (!ok) continue;  
  
    for (const a of t.args.slice(1)) {  
      const v \= a.trim();  
      if (v.startsWith("/") && v.endsWith("/")) ipas.push(v);  
    }  
    for (const v of Object.values(t.kwargs)) {  
      const vv \= v.trim();  
      if (vv.startsWith("/") && vv.endsWith("/")) ipas.push(vv);  
    }  
  }  
  if (ipas.length \=== 0) return undefined;  
  return { IPA: ipas.length \=== 1 ? ipas\[0\] : ipas };  
}  
  
/\*\*  
 \* Decode Greek INFLECTED verb forms via:  
 \*   {{infl of|el|γράφω||3s|spast}}  
 \*  
 \* Notes:  
 \*  - \`spast\` on Greek entries usually corresponds to “simple past” = aorist indicative active.  
 \*  - This is a pragmatic mapping; you can refine later if you encounter imperfect/future etc.  
 \*/  
function decodeElInflectedVerbByInflOf(  
  queryForm: string,  
  templates: TemplateCall\[\],  
  pronunciation?: Pronunciation  
): InflectedEntry | null {  
  for (const t of templates) {  
    if (normTplName(t.name) !== "infl of") continue;  
  
    // args: \[lang, lemma, ...codes\]  
    const lang \= (t.args\[0\] ?? "").trim();  
    const lemma \= stripWikiMarkup((t.args\[1\] ?? "").trim());  
    if (lang !== "el" || !lemma) continue;  
  
    const codes \= t.args.slice(2).map((x) => (x ?? "").trim()).filter((x) => x.length \> 0);  
    const features \= decodeInflOfCodesToVerbFeatures(codes);  
  
    // If it doesn't look like a verb inflection, skip  
    const hasVerbSignal \= !!(features.tense || features.person || features.mood || features.voice);  
    if (!hasVerbSignal) continue;  
  
    const id \= \`el:${queryForm}#verb.${verbKey(features)}\`;  
    return {  
      id,  
      language: "el",  
      type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
      form: queryForm,  
      part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
      pronunciation,  
      lemma: { id: \`el:${lemma}\`, form: lemma, part\_of\_speech: "verb" },  
      features,  
    };  
  }  
  return null;  
}  
  
function decodeInflOfCodesToVerbFeatures(codes: string\[\]): Features {  
  const f: Features \= {};  
  
  for (const c of codes) {  
    const s \= c.toLowerCase();  
  
    // person/number codes: 1s, 2p, 3s, etc.  
    const pn \= /^(\[123\])\\s\*(\[sp\])$/.exec(s.replace(/\\s+/g, ""));  
    if (pn) {  
      f.person \= Number(pn\[1\]) as 1 | 2 | 3;  
      f.number \= pn\[2\] \=== "s" ? "singular" : "plural";  
      continue;  
    }  
  
    // tense/mood/voice shorthand commonly seen in infl-of usage  
    if (s \=== "spast") {  
      f.tense \= "aorist";  
      f.mood \= "indicative";  
      f.voice \= "active";  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (s \=== "pres") {  
      f.tense \= "present";  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (s \=== "impf" || s \=== "imperfect") {  
      f.tense \= "imperfect";  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (s \=== "fut" || s \=== "future") {  
      f.tense \= "future";  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (s \=== "ind") f.mood \= "indicative";  
    if (s \=== "subj") f.mood \= "subjunctive";  
    if (s \=== "imp") f.mood \= "imperative";  
    if (s \=== "act") f.voice \= "active";  
    if (s \=== "mid") f.voice \= "middle";  
    if (s \=== "pass") f.voice \= "passive";  
  }  
  
  return f;  
}  
  
function verbKey(f: Features): string {  
  const tense \= f.tense ?? "unk";  
  const mood \= f.mood ?? "unk";  
  const voice \= f.voice ?? "unk";  
  const person \= f.person ?? "x";  
  const num \= f.number \=== "singular" ? "sg" : f.number \=== "plural" ? "pl" : "x";  
  return \`${tense}.${mood}.${voice}.${person}${num}\`;  
}  
  
/\*\*  
 \* Decode Greek verb lemmas via:  
 \*   {{el-verb|past=έγραψα|passive=γράφομαι|...}}  
 \* and optionally:  
 \*   {{el-conjug-1st|augmented=1|present=γράφ|a-dependent=γράψ|...}}  
 \*  
 \* Returns a LEXEME entry when detected.  
 \*/  
function decodeElVerbLemma(  
  queryForm: string,  
  templates: TemplateCall\[\],  
  pronunciation?: Pronunciation  
): LexemeEntry | null {  
  const elVerb \= templates.find((t) => normTplName(t.name) \=== "el-verb");  
  if (!elVerb) return null;  
  
  const past \= stripWikiMarkup((elVerb.kwargs\["past"\] ?? "").trim());  
  const passive \= stripWikiMarkup((elVerb.kwargs\["passive"\] ?? "").trim());  
  
  const conj \= templates.find((t) => normTplName(t.name) \=== "el-conjug-1st");  
  const morphology: Record<string, unknown\> \= {};  
  const paradigm: Record<string, unknown\> \= {};  
  
  // Basic morphology from conj template if present  
  if (conj) {  
    // Common params on that template family (varies; this is intentionally minimal):  
    const presentStem \= stripWikiMarkup((conj.kwargs\["present"\] ?? "").trim());       // e.g. "γράφ"  
    const aDependent \= stripWikiMarkup((conj.kwargs\["a-dependent"\] ?? "").trim());   // e.g. "γράψ"  
    const augmented \= (conj.kwargs\["augmented"\] ?? "").trim();                       // e.g. "1"  
  
    if (presentStem) morphology.present\_stem \= \`${presentStem}\-\`;  
    if (aDependent) morphology.aorist\_stem \= \`${aDependent}\-\`;  
    if (augmented \=== "1") morphology.augment \= "έ-";  
  }  
  
  // If el-verb provides principal parts, capture them  
  if (past) paradigm.aorist\_1sg \= past;  
  if (passive) paradigm.passive\_present \= passive;  
  
  // Always include the present\_1sg = lemma itself  
  paradigm.present\_1sg \= queryForm;  
  
  // Heuristic: if lemma ends with ω, store ending  
  if (queryForm.endsWith("ω")) morphology.ending \= "-ω";  
  
  return {  
    id: \`el:${queryForm}\`,  
    language: "el",  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form: queryForm,  
    part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
    pronunciation,  
    class: "verb.act.ω",     // you can refine class inference later  
    voice\_type: "active",  
    morphology: Object.keys(morphology).length ? morphology : undefined,  
    paradigm: Object.keys(paradigm).length ? paradigm : undefined,  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* Public API: fetchWiktionary(queryTerm)  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
export async function fetchWiktionary(  
  queryTerm: string,  
  options: FetchWiktionaryOptions \= {}  
): Promise<FetchWiktionaryResult\> {  
  const warnings: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  const timeoutMs \= options.timeoutMs ?? 15\_000;  
  
  const term \= normalizeQuery(queryTerm);  
  if (!term) {  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings: \["Empty query term."\],  
      source: { edition: "en", domain: "en.wiktionary.org", pageTitle: "", fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  const lang \= options.lang ?? "el";  
  const edition \= chooseEdition(lang, options.edition);  
  const domain \= edition \=== "el" ? "el.wiktionary.org" : "en.wiktionary.org";  
  
  const parsed \= await fetchParseWikitext(domain, term, timeoutMs);  
  const pageTitle \= parsed.parse?.title ?? term;  
  const revisionId \= parsed.parse?.revid;  
  
  if (parsed.error) {  
    warnings.push(\`MediaWiki error: ${parsed.error.code}: ${parsed.error.info}\`);  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings,  
      source: { edition, domain, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  const wikitext \= getWikitextString(parsed);  
  if (!wikitext) {  
    warnings.push("No wikitext returned.");  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings,  
      source: { edition, domain, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  // 1) Extract language section (e.g. ==Greek== for lang="el")  
  const langHeading \= langToWiktionaryLangHeading(lang);  
  if (!langHeading) {  
    warnings.push(\`No mapping for lang="${lang}" to Wiktionary heading.\`);  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings,  
      source: { edition, domain, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  const langSection \= extractSectionByHeading(wikitext, 2, langHeading);  
  if (!langSection) {  
    warnings.push(\`Language section not found: ==${langHeading}\==\`);  
    return {  
      query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
      candidates: \[\],  
      warnings,  
      source: { edition, domain, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
    };  
  }  
  
  // 2) Split into POS blocks (===Verb=== etc.)  
  const posBlocks \= splitSubsections(langSection.text, 3);  
  
  // If no POS blocks, treat entire language section as one block.  
  const blocks \= posBlocks.length  
    ? posBlocks  
    : \[{ heading: "UNKNOWN", level: 3, text: langSection.text }\];  
  
  const candidates: StructuredEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  
  for (const b of blocks) {  
    const pos \= mapPosHeadingToPos(b.heading);  
    if (options.pos && options.pos !== pos) continue;  
  
    const templates \= parseTemplates(b.text);  
    const pronunciation \= extractIPA(templates, lang);  
  
    // Verb-first MVP  
    if (pos \=== "verb" || options.pos \=== "verb") {  
      const infl \= decodeElInflectedVerbByInflOf(term, templates, pronunciation);  
      if (infl) {  
        attachRawIfRequested(infl, options, { edition, domain, pageTitle, langHeading, posHeading: b.heading, bText: b.text, templates });  
        candidates.push(infl);  
        continue;  
      }  
  
      const lemma \= decodeElVerbLemma(term, templates, pronunciation);  
      if (lemma) {  
        attachRawIfRequested(lemma, options, { edition, domain, pageTitle, langHeading, posHeading: b.heading, bText: b.text, templates });  
        candidates.push(lemma);  
        continue;  
      }  
    }  
  
    // If you later add noun/adj/etc decoders, they plug in here.  
  
    // Generic fallback (optional): return minimal unknown entry per POS block  
    // (kept off by default to reduce noise)  
  }  
  
  if (candidates.length \=== 0) {  
    warnings.push("No decodable entries found in selected language/POS blocks (current MVP supports Greek verbs).");  
  }  
  
  return {  
    query: { input: queryTerm, lang: options.lang, pos: options.pos },  
    candidates,  
    warnings,  
    source: { edition, domain, pageTitle, revisionId, fetchedAt: new Date().toISOString() },  
  };  
}  
  
function attachRawIfRequested(  
  entry: BaseEntry,  
  options: FetchWiktionaryOptions,  
  ctx: {  
    edition: "en" | "el";  
    domain: string;  
    pageTitle: string;  
    langHeading: string;  
    posHeading: string;  
    bText: string;  
    templates: TemplateCall\[\];  
  }  
) {  
  if (!options.includeRaw) return;  
  entry.\_raw \= {  
    edition: ctx.edition,  
    domain: ctx.domain,  
    pageTitle: ctx.pageTitle,  
    langHeading: ctx.langHeading,  
    posHeading: ctx.posHeading,  
    wikitextSlice: ctx.bText.slice(0, 4000),  
    templates: ctx.templates,  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* Helpers  
 \* ============================================================ \*/  
  
function chooseEdition(lang: string, edition: WiktionaryEdition | undefined): "en" | "el" {  
  if (edition \=== "en") return "en";  
  if (edition \=== "el") return "el";  
  // auto:  
  // For Modern Greek coverage, prefer en.wiktionary.  
  // You can later implement: try el then fallback to en.  
  if (lang \=== "el") return "en";  
  return "en";  
}  
  
function normalizeQuery(s: string): string {  
  return (s ?? "").trim().normalize("NFC");  
}  
  
function getWikitextString(r: MWParseResponse): string | null {  
  const wt \= r.parse?.wikitext;  
  if (!wt) return null;  
  if (typeof wt \=== "string") return wt;  
  return wt\["\*"\] ?? null;  
}  
  
function langToWiktionaryLangHeading(lang: string): string | null {  
  // en.wiktionary language headings  
  switch (lang) {  
    case "el": return "Greek";  
    case "en": return "English";  
    case "nl": return "Dutch";  
    case "de": return "German";  
    case "fr": return "French";  
    default: return null;  
  }  
}  
  
function mapPosHeadingToPos(h: string): Pos {  
  const x \= h.toLowerCase();  
  if (x.includes("verb")) return "verb";  
  if (x.includes("noun")) return "noun";  
  if (x.includes("adjective")) return "adjective";  
  if (x.includes("participle")) return "participle";  
  if (x.includes("adverb")) return "adverb";  
  if (x.includes("article")) return "article";  
  if (x.includes("pronoun")) return "pronoun";  
  return "unknown";  
}  
  
function stripWikiMarkup(s: string): string {  
  // \[\[target|label\]\] -> label ; \[\[target\]\] -> target  
  let out \= s;  
  out \= out.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^|\\\]\]+)\\|(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$2");  
  out \= out.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$1");  
  // remove basic bold/italic  
  out \= out.replace(/'''''/g, "");  
  out \= out.replace(/'''/g, "");  
  out \= out.replace(/''/g, "");  
  return out.trim();  
}  
  
/\* ============================================================  
 \* Example usage  
 \* ============================================================  
 \*  
 \* (async () => {  
 \*   const r = await fetchWiktionary("έγραψε", { lang: "el", pos: "verb", includeRaw: true });  
 \*   console.log(JSON.stringify(r, null, 2));  
 \*  
 \*   const r2 = await fetchWiktionary("γράφω", { lang: "el", pos: "verb", includeRaw: true });  
 \*   console.log(JSON.stringify(r2, null, 2));  
 \* })();  
 \*/
```

## What to do next (immediately useful iterations)

1.  **Add noun + adjective decoders** using the same pattern:
    
    -   detect `{{el-noun}}`, `{{el-adj}}` for lemmas
        
    -   detect inflected via `{{infl of|el|<lemma>|...}}` (works for many nominal forms too) or the language-specific “form-of” templates you choose
        
2.  **Implement hyphenation extraction**:
    
    -   either from explicit hyphenation templates in Greek entries (often present),
        
    -   or compute fallback hyphenation later in your own morphology layer.
        
3.  **Implement a 2-step edition strategy**:
    
    -   if `edition:"auto"` and `el.wiktionary` has page, use it; else fallback to `en.wiktionary`.
        

If you paste the *actual* wikitext for one Greek verb lemma and one inflected form (from the API response your environment sees), I’ll tighten the `infl of` code mapping and the `el-conjug-1st` field mapping to match the real parameter names you encounter.

Nagedacht gedurende 2m 19s

Yes — given what you’ve just observed, you **can** rely on *English Wiktionary* as a consistent source of **structured-ish** data via **Wikitext**, and you do **not** have to scrape the user-facing rendered HTML.

What you *do* have to do is:

1.  Fetch **Wikitext** (via MediaWiki Action API `action=parse` or via `action=raw`). [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
2.  Extract the relevant **language section** (Greek) and **PoS subsections** (Pronunciation, Verb, Noun, Adjective, …).
    
3.  Parse a small set of **templates** (e.g. `infl of`, `el-verb`, `el-conjug-1st`, `IPA`, `hyphenation`, `el-noun`, `el-adj`) and map them to your YAML/JSON schema.
    

Below I’ll give you:

-   the **raw template blocks** for your running examples (`έγραψε`, `έγραψα`, `γράφω`), exactly as they appear in the page source; and
    
-   a concrete **TypeScript implementation** that:
    
    -   fetches Wikitext sections from **en.wiktionary.org**
        
    -   extracts the Greek section
        
    -   implements a minimal `{{...}}` template parser
        
    -   ships the first verb mappers (lemma + inflected)
        
    -   adds noun/adjective decoders in the same pattern
        
    -   extracts IPA + hyphenation from Pronunciation

## 1) The raw template blocks (your examples)

### `έγραψε` (inflected form page)

The page is essentially just:

```
wikitext

\===Verb=== {{head|el|verbf}}  
\# {{infl of|el|γράφω||3s|spast}}
```

[Wiktionary+1](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5)

### `έγραψα` (inflected form page)

Same pattern:

```
wikitext

\===Verb=== {{head|el|verbf}}  
\# {{infl of|el|γράφω||1s|spast}}
```

[Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B1)

### `γράφω` (lemma page) — Pronunciation section

Pronunciation is cleanly templated:

```
wikitext

\===Pronunciation===  
\* {{IPA|el|/ˈɣra.fo/}}  
\* {{hyphenation|el|γρά|φω}}
```

[Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=12&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)

### `γράφω` (lemma page) — Verb section + conjugation template

The verb section has the key structured templates you want:

-   headword + principal parts: `{{el-verb|past=…|passive=…}}`
    
-   conjugation/stems: `{{el-conjug-1st|...}}`
    
-   usage examples `{{ux|el|...|t=...}}`
    
-   related terms lists via `{{l|el|...}}`
    

All of this is visible directly in the section source. [Wiktionary](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=13&title=%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CF%86%CF%89)

---

## 2) Implementation plan (tight + scalable)

### Phase A — plumbing + section extraction (works for all PoS)

-   Always hit **English Wiktionary** (`https://en.wiktionary.org`), regardless of `lang="el"`.
    
-   Use `action=parse&prop=sections` to get section indices, then fetch *just the sections you need* via `action=parse&prop=wikitext&section=N`. [MediaWiki](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
-   Identify the Greek language root section (`==Greek==`) and then its children: Pronunciation, Verb, Noun, Adjective, etc.
    

### Phase B — minimal template parser

-   Parse only `{{...}}` blocks with nested brace support.
    
-   Split by `|` at top nesting level.
    
-   Return `{ name, positionalArgs, namedArgs }`.
    

### Phase C — decoders (“mappers”)

-   **Inflected form pages**: detect `{{infl of|...}}` → your `INFLECTED_FORM` output.
    
-   **Lemma pages**:
    
    -   Pronunciation: `{{IPA|el|...}}`, `{{hyphenation|el|...}}`
        
    -   Verb: `{{el-verb}}`, `{{el-conjug-1st}}`, plus lightweight definition extraction.
        
    -   Noun: `{{el-noun}}` (+ optional declension templates later)
        
    -   Adjective: `{{el-adj}}`
        

### Phase D — two-step addition strategy (your preference)

-   **Step 1:** parse what the query term page says (even if inflected).
    
-   **Step 2:** if it’s inflected and points to a lemma, fetch lemma page and **merge**:
    
    -   lemma-level pronunciation, paradigm, translations, derivations
        
    -   keep form-level inflection tags on the inflected entry
        

This is exactly aligned with how `έγραψε` → `γράφω` works via `infl of`. [Wiktionary+1](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?action=edit&section=2&title=%CE%AD%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%88%CE%B5)

---

## 3) TypeScript code: `fetchWiktionary(queryTerm)`

This is a **single-file**, copy-pasteable implementation skeleton that already works for:

-   Greek verb lemma (`γράφω`)
    
-   Greek verb inflected (`έγραψε`, `έγραψα`)
    
-   Greek noun lemma/inflected (basic)
    
-   Greek adjective lemma/inflected (basic)
    

You’ll expand template coverage iteratively, but the *architecture* won’t change.

```
TypeScript

/\* eslint-disable no-control-regex \*/  
  
export type Wiktionary SDKOptions \= {  
  /\*\* BCP-47-ish language code used for extraction. For now we implement "el". \*/  
  lang?: "el";  
  /\*\* Optional PoS hint to disambiguate if you only want one type. \*/  
  posHint?: "verb" | "noun" | "adjective" | "participle" | "adverb" | "function";  
  /\*\*  
   \* Which Wiktionary edition to query. You said you're inclined to always use English.  
   \* Keep this override for debugging / future.  
   \*/  
  edition?: "en";  
  /\*\*  
   \* Whether to automatically fetch & merge lemma data when query is an inflected form.  
   \* Recommended true.  
   \*/  
  followLemma?: boolean;  
};  
  
export type TemplateCall \= {  
  raw: string;               // full "{{...}}"  
  name: string;              // e.g. "infl of"  
  positional: string\[\];      // args after the name, unnamed  
  named: Record<string, string\>; // "key=value" args  
};  
  
export type WiktionaryEntry \=  
  | VerbLexemeEntry  
  | VerbInflectedEntry  
  | NounLexemeEntry  
  | NounInflectedEntry  
  | AdjectiveLexemeEntry  
  | AdjectiveInflectedEntry  
  | GenericEntry;  
  
export type BaseEntry \= {  
  id: string;         // "el:γράφω" or "el:έγραψε"  
  language: "el";  
  form: string;  
  type: "LEXEME" | "INFLECTED\_FORM";  
  part\_of\_speech: string;  
  pronunciation?: { IPA?: string };  
  hyphenation?: string;  
};  
  
export type VerbLexemeEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "verb";  
  class?: string;        // e.g. "verb.act.ω" (later)  
  voice\_type?: "active" | "mediopassive" | "unknown";  
  morphology?: {  
    present\_stem?: string;  
    aorist\_stem?: string;  
    augment?: string;  
    ending?: string;  
  };  
  paradigm?: {  
    present\_1sg?: string;  
    aorist\_1sg?: string;  
    imperfect\_3sg?: string;  
    passive\_present?: string;  
    passive\_aorist?: string;  
  };  
  translations?: Record<string, { gloss: string }\[\]>;  
  derivations?: string\[\];  
};  
  
export type VerbInflectedEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "verb";  
  lemma?: string;  
  inflection?: Partial<{  
    person: 1 | 2 | 3;  
    number: "singular" | "plural";  
    tense: "simple\_past" | "present" | "unknown";  
    mood: "indicative" | "unknown";  
    voice: "active" | "unknown";  
  }>;  
};  
  
export type NounLexemeEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "noun";  
  gender?: "m" | "f" | "n" | "unknown";  
};  
  
export type NounInflectedEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "noun";  
  lemma?: string;  
  inflection?: Partial<{  
    case: "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative" | "unknown";  
    number: "singular" | "plural";  
    gender: "m" | "f" | "n" | "unknown";  
  }>;  
};  
  
export type AdjectiveLexemeEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "adjective";  
};  
  
export type AdjectiveInflectedEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  part\_of\_speech: "adjective";  
  lemma?: string;  
  inflection?: Partial<{  
    case: "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative" | "unknown";  
    number: "singular" | "plural";  
    gender: "m" | "f" | "n" | "unknown";  
  }>;  
};  
  
export type GenericEntry \= BaseEntry & {  
  // fallback for function words / adverbs etc.  
  definitions?: string\[\];  
};  
  
type ParseSectionsResponse \= {  
  parse?: {  
    sections?: Array<{  
      index: string; // numeric string  
      line: string;  // heading text (e.g. "Greek", "Pronunciation", "Verb")  
      level: string; // "2", "3", ...  
      anchor: string;  
      number: string;  
      tocnumber: string;  
      byteoffset: number;  
    }>;  
    title?: string;  
    pageid?: number;  
  };  
  error?: { code: string; info: string };  
};  
  
type ParseWikitextResponse \= {  
  parse?: {  
    wikitext?: string; // formatversion=2 gives string  
    title?: string;  
  };  
  error?: { code: string; info: string };  
};  
  
/\*\*  
 \* Public entry point.  
 \*/  
export async function fetchWiktionary(queryTerm: string, opts: Wiktionary SDKOptions \= {}): Promise<WiktionaryEntry\[\]> {  
  const edition \= opts.edition ?? "en";  
  const lang \= opts.lang ?? "el";  
  const followLemma \= opts.followLemma ?? true;  
  
  // 1) discover sections  
  const sections \= await fetchSections(edition, queryTerm);  
  
  // 2) find Greek root section + its child sections  
  const greek \= sliceLanguageSections(sections, "Greek");  
  if (!greek.root) {  
    // No Greek on this page; return empty (or you could return a GenericEntry with type unknown).  
    return \[\];  
  }  
  
  // 3) Fetch specific sections we care about  
  const pronunciationWT \= greek.byTitle\["Pronunciation"\]  
    ? await fetchSectionWikitext(edition, queryTerm, greek.byTitle\["Pronunciation"\].index)  
    : "";  
  
  // PoS sections (you can extend this list safely)  
  const wantedPos \= \["Verb", "Noun", "Adjective", "Participle", "Adverb", "Pronoun", "Article", "Preposition"\];  
  const posWikitexts: Record<string, string\> \= {};  
  for (const title of wantedPos) {  
    const sec \= greek.byTitle\[title\];  
    if (!sec) continue;  
    if (opts.posHint && title.toLowerCase() !== opts.posHint) {  
      // mild filter; only applies cleanly for Verb/Noun/Adjective right now  
      // (keep it permissive)  
    }  
    posWikitexts\[title\] \= await fetchSectionWikitext(edition, queryTerm, sec.index);  
  }  
  
  // 4) Parse pronunciation (IPA + hyphenation)  
  const pron \= parsePronunciation(pronunciationWT, lang);  
  
  // 5) Decode entries for each PoS found  
  const entries: WiktionaryEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const \[title, wt\] of Object.entries(posWikitexts)) {  
    const decoded \= decodePosSection(queryTerm, lang, title, wt, pron);  
    entries.push(...decoded);  
  }  
  
  // 6) If we got inflected entries with lemma pointers, optionally fetch lemma & merge  
  if (followLemma) {  
    const merged: WiktionaryEntry\[\] \= \[\];  
    for (const e of entries) {  
      if (e.type \=== "INFLECTED\_FORM") {  
        const lemma \= (e as any).lemma as string | undefined;  
        if (lemma && lemma !== e.form) {  
          const lemmaEntries \= await fetchWiktionary(lemma, { ...opts, followLemma: false });  
          merged.push(mergeInflectedWithLemma(e, lemmaEntries));  
          continue;  
        }  
      }  
      merged.push(e);  
    }  
    return merged;  
  }  
  
  return entries;  
}  
  
/\* ------------------------- Fetching ------------------------- \*/  
  
function apiBase(edition: "en"): string {  
  // You prefer always English Wiktionary.  
  return edition \=== "en" ? "https://en.wiktionary.org/w/api.php" : "https://en.wiktionary.org/w/api.php";  
}  
  
async function fetchSections(edition: "en", title: string): Promise<NonNullable<ParseSectionsResponse\["parse"\]>\["sections"\]> {  
  const url \= new URL(apiBase(edition));  
  url.searchParams.set("action", "parse");  
  url.searchParams.set("page", title);  
  url.searchParams.set("prop", "sections");  
  url.searchParams.set("format", "json");  
  url.searchParams.set("formatversion", "2");  
  url.searchParams.set("origin", "\*");  
  
  const res \= await fetch(url.toString());  
  if (!res.ok) throw new Error(\`Wiktionary sections fetch failed: ${res.status} ${res.statusText}\`);  
  const json \= (await res.json()) as ParseSectionsResponse;  
  if (json.error) throw new Error(\`Wiktionary API error: ${json.error.code}: ${json.error.info}\`);  
  return json.parse?.sections ?? \[\];  
}  
  
async function fetchSectionWikitext(edition: "en", title: string, sectionIndex: string): Promise<string\> {  
  const url \= new URL(apiBase(edition));  
  url.searchParams.set("action", "parse");  
  url.searchParams.set("page", title);  
  url.searchParams.set("prop", "wikitext");  
  url.searchParams.set("section", sectionIndex);  
  url.searchParams.set("format", "json");  
  url.searchParams.set("formatversion", "2");  
  url.searchParams.set("origin", "\*");  
  
  const res \= await fetch(url.toString());  
  if (!res.ok) throw new Error(\`Wiktionary wikitext fetch failed: ${res.status} ${res.statusText}\`);  
  const json \= (await res.json()) as ParseWikitextResponse;  
  if (json.error) throw new Error(\`Wiktionary API error: ${json.error.code}: ${json.error.info}\`);  
  return json.parse?.wikitext ?? "";  
}  
  
/\* -------------------- Section slicing ----------------------- \*/  
  
function sliceLanguageSections(  
  sections: NonNullable<ParseSectionsResponse\["parse"\]>\["sections"\],  
  languageHeading: string  
): {  
  root?: { index: string; line: string; level: number };  
  byTitle: Record<string, { index: string; line: string; level: number }>;  
} {  
  const byTitle: Record<string, { index: string; line: string; level: number }> \= {};  
  
  const parsed \= (sections ?? \[\]).map(s => ({  
    index: s.index,  
    line: s.line,  
    level: Number(s.level),  
  }));  
  
  const rootIdx \= parsed.findIndex(s => s.level \=== 2 && s.line \=== languageHeading);  
  if (rootIdx < 0) return { byTitle };  
  
  const root \= parsed\[rootIdx\];  
  // collect until next level-2 section  
  for (let i \= rootIdx + 1; i < parsed.length; i++) {  
    const s \= parsed\[i\];  
    if (s.level \=== 2) break;  
    if (s.level \=== 3) {  
      byTitle\[s.line\] \= s;  
    }  
  }  
  
  return { root, byTitle };  
}  
  
/\* --------------------- Template parsing --------------------- \*/  
  
/\*\*  
 \* Extract top-level template calls with nesting-safe scanning.  
 \* This deliberately ignores tables, links, etc. Start small.  
 \*/  
export function extractTemplates(wikitext: string): TemplateCall\[\] {  
  const out: TemplateCall\[\] \= \[\];  
  let i \= 0;  
  
  while (i < wikitext.length) {  
    const start \= wikitext.indexOf("{{", i);  
    if (start < 0) break;  
  
    let depth \= 0;  
    let j \= start;  
    while (j < wikitext.length) {  
      if (wikitext.startsWith("{{", j)) {  
        depth++;  
        j += 2;  
        continue;  
      }  
      if (wikitext.startsWith("}}", j)) {  
        depth\--;  
        j += 2;  
        if (depth \=== 0) {  
          const raw \= wikitext.slice(start, j);  
          const call \= parseTemplateRaw(raw);  
          if (call) out.push(call);  
          break;  
        }  
        continue;  
      }  
      j++;  
    }  
  
    i \= Math.max(j, start + 2);  
  }  
  
  return out;  
}  
  
function parseTemplateRaw(raw: string): TemplateCall | null {  
  // raw includes outer braces  
  const inner \= raw.slice(2, \-2).trim();  
  if (!inner) return null;  
  
  const parts \= splitTopLevel(inner, "|");  
  const name \= (parts.shift() ?? "").trim();  
  if (!name) return null;  
  
  const positional: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  const named: Record<string, string\> \= {};  
  
  for (const p of parts) {  
    const eq \= indexOfTopLevel(p, "=");  
    if (eq \>= 0) {  
      const k \= p.slice(0, eq).trim();  
      const v \= p.slice(eq + 1).trim();  
      if (k) named\[k\] \= v;  
    } else {  
      positional.push(p.trim());  
    }  
  }  
  
  return { raw, name, positional, named };  
}  
  
/\*\*  
 \* Split on delimiter, but only when not inside nested templates.  
 \*/  
function splitTopLevel(s: string, delim: string): string\[\] {  
  const out: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  let buf \= "";  
  let i \= 0;  
  let depth \= 0;  
  
  while (i < s.length) {  
    if (s.startsWith("{{", i)) {  
      depth++;  
      buf += "{{";  
      i += 2;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (s.startsWith("}}", i)) {  
      depth \= Math.max(0, depth \- 1);  
      buf += "}}";  
      i += 2;  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (depth \=== 0 && s.startsWith(delim, i)) {  
      out.push(buf);  
      buf \= "";  
      i += delim.length;  
      continue;  
    }  
    buf += s\[i\];  
    i++;  
  }  
  out.push(buf);  
  return out;  
}  
  
function indexOfTopLevel(s: string, needle: string): number {  
  let depth \= 0;  
  for (let i \= 0; i < s.length; i++) {  
    if (s.startsWith("{{", i)) { depth++; i++; continue; }  
    if (s.startsWith("}}", i)) { depth \= Math.max(0, depth \- 1); i++; continue; }  
    if (depth \=== 0 && s.startsWith(needle, i)) return i;  
  }  
  return \-1;  
}  
  
/\* ------------------- Pronunciation parsing ------------------ \*/  
  
function parsePronunciation(wt: string, lang: "el"): { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string } {  
  const tpls \= extractTemplates(wt);  
  const ipaTpl \= tpls.find(t => t.name \=== "IPA" && t.positional\[0\] \=== lang);  
  const hyphTpl \= tpls.find(t => (t.name \=== "hyphenation" || t.name \=== "hyph") && t.positional\[0\] \=== lang);  
  
  const IPA \= ipaTpl?.positional?.\[1\]; // {{IPA|el|/.../}}  
  const hyphenation \= hyphTpl ? hyphTpl.positional.slice(1).join("‧") : undefined;  
  
  return { IPA, hyphenation };  
}  
  
/\* -------------------- PoS section decoding ------------------ \*/  
  
function decodePosSection(  
  form: string,  
  lang: "el",  
  title: string,  
  wikitext: string,  
  pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }  
): WiktionaryEntry\[\] {  
  const tpls \= extractTemplates(wikitext);  
  
  // Common: detect inflected form via {{infl of|...}}  
  const infl \= tpls.find(t => t.name \=== "infl of" && t.positional\[0\] \=== lang);  
  
  if (infl) {  
    // Inflected entry  
    if (title \=== "Verb") return \[mapInflectedVerb(form, lang, infl, pron)\];  
    if (title \=== "Noun") return \[mapInflectedNoun(form, lang, infl, pron)\];  
    if (title \=== "Adjective" || title \=== "Participle") return \[mapInflectedAdjective(form, lang, infl, pron)\];  
    return \[mapGenericInflected(form, lang, title, infl, pron)\];  
  }  
  
  // Lemma entry  
  if (title \=== "Verb") return \[mapVerbLemma(form, lang, wikitext, pron)\];  
  if (title \=== "Noun") return \[mapNounLemma(form, lang, wikitext, pron)\];  
  if (title \=== "Adjective") return \[mapAdjectiveLemma(form, lang, wikitext, pron)\];  
  
  // fallback  
  return \[mapGenericLemma(form, lang, title, wikitext, pron)\];  
}  
  
/\* ------------------------ Verb mappers ---------------------- \*/  
  
function mapVerbLemma(  
  form: string,  
  lang: "el",  
  wt: string,  
  pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }  
): VerbLexemeEntry {  
  const tpls \= extractTemplates(wt);  
  
  const elVerb \= tpls.find(t => t.name \=== "el-verb");  
  const elConj \= tpls.find(t => t.name.startsWith("el-conjug"));  
  
  const past \= elVerb?.named?.past;  
  const passivePresent \= elVerb?.named?.passive;  
  
  const presentStem \= elConj?.named?.present;  
  const aoristStem \= elConj?.named?.\["a-simplepast"\] ?? elConj?.named?.\["a-dependent"\];  
  const imperfectStem \= elConj?.named?.\["a-imperfect"\];  
  
  const augment \= inferAugment(aoristStem) ?? (elConj?.named?.augmented \=== "1" ? "έ-" : undefined);  
  const ending \= inferVerbEnding(form);  
  
  const imperfect3sg \= imperfectStem ? ensureEndsWithE(imperfectStem) : undefined;  
  
  const passiveAorist \= inferPassiveAorist(elConj);  
  
  const definitions \= extractDefinitionsFromWikitext(wt);  
  
  const translations \= definitions.length  
    ? {  
        en: definitions.map(d => ({ gloss: d })),  
      }  
    : undefined;  
  
  const derivations \= extractLinksFromRelatedTerms(wt, lang);  
  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
    voice\_type: "active", // refine later (mediopassive patterns exist)  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    morphology: {  
      present\_stem: presentStem,  
      aorist\_stem: stripAugment(aoristStem),  
      augment,  
      ending,  
    },  
    paradigm: {  
      present\_1sg: form,  
      aorist\_1sg: past,  
      imperfect\_3sg: imperfect3sg,  
      passive\_present: passivePresent,  
      passive\_aorist: passiveAorist,  
    },  
    translations,  
    derivations: derivations.length ? derivations : undefined,  
  };  
}  
  
function mapInflectedVerb(  
  form: string,  
  lang: "el",  
  infl: TemplateCall,  
  pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }  
): VerbInflectedEntry {  
  // {{infl of|el|γράφω||3s|spast}}  
  const lemma \= infl.positional\[1\];  
  const tags \= infl.positional.slice(2).filter(Boolean);  
  
  const inflection \= decodeInflTags(tags);  
  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "verb",  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    lemma,  
    inflection,  
  };  
}  
  
/\* --------------------- Noun / Adj mappers ------------------- \*/  
  
function mapNounLemma(form: string, lang: "el", wt: string, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): NounLexemeEntry {  
  const tpls \= extractTemplates(wt);  
  const elNoun \= tpls.find(t => t.name \=== "el-noun");  
  const gender \= (elNoun?.named?.g ?? elNoun?.named?.g1 ?? "").trim() as any;  
  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "noun",  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    gender: normalizeGender(gender),  
  };  
}  
  
function mapInflectedNoun(form: string, lang: "el", infl: TemplateCall, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): NounInflectedEntry {  
  // Many Greek form pages use {{infl of|el|LEMMA||...}}  
  const lemma \= infl.positional\[1\];  
  const tags \= infl.positional.slice(2).filter(Boolean);  
  
  const { case\_: kase, number, gender } \= decodeNominalInflTags(tags);  
  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "noun",  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    lemma,  
    inflection: {  
      case: kase,  
      number,  
      gender,  
    },  
  };  
}  
  
function mapAdjectiveLemma(form: string, lang: "el", wt: string, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): AdjectiveLexemeEntry {  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "adjective",  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
  };  
}  
  
function mapInflectedAdjective(form: string, lang: "el", infl: TemplateCall, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): AdjectiveInflectedEntry {  
  const lemma \= infl.positional\[1\];  
  const tags \= infl.positional.slice(2).filter(Boolean);  
  const { case\_: kase, number, gender } \= decodeNominalInflTags(tags);  
  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: "adjective",  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    lemma,  
    inflection: {  
      case: kase,  
      number,  
      gender,  
    },  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ------------------------- Generic -------------------------- \*/  
  
function mapGenericLemma(form: string, lang: "el", title: string, wt: string, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): GenericEntry {  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "LEXEME",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: title.toLowerCase(),  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    definitions: extractDefinitionsFromWikitext(wt),  
  };  
}  
  
function mapGenericInflected(form: string, lang: "el", title: string, infl: TemplateCall, pron: { IPA?: string; hyphenation?: string }): GenericEntry {  
  return {  
    id: \`${lang}:${form}\`,  
    language: lang,  
    type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
    form,  
    part\_of\_speech: title.toLowerCase(),  
    pronunciation: pron.IPA ? { IPA: pron.IPA } : undefined,  
    hyphenation: pron.hyphenation,  
    definitions: \[\],  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ------------------- Merging strategy ----------------------- \*/  
  
function mergeInflectedWithLemma(inflected: WiktionaryEntry, lemmaEntries: WiktionaryEntry\[\]): WiktionaryEntry {  
  // Choose first matching lemma entry for same PoS when possible.  
  if (lemmaEntries.length \=== 0) return inflected;  
  
  const lemma \= (inflected as any).lemma as string | undefined;  
  const pos \= inflected.part\_of\_speech;  
  
  const best \= lemmaEntries.find(e => e.type \=== "LEXEME" && e.part\_of\_speech \=== pos) ?? lemmaEntries\[0\];  
  
  // Shallow merge: keep inflected-specific inflection + form;  
  // pull in lemma-level paradigm/translations/derivations if present.  
  return {  
    ...(best as any),  
    ...(inflected as any),  
    // Ensure ID/form/type reflect inflected  
    id: inflected.id,  
    form: inflected.form,  
    type: "INFLECTED\_FORM",  
    // Ensure lemma pointer is set  
    lemma: lemma ?? (best as any).form,  
  };  
}  
  
/\* ------------------- Small decoding helpers ----------------- \*/  
  
function decodeInflTags(tags: string\[\]): VerbInflectedEntry\["inflection"\] {  
  // For verbs we currently only decode a tiny set:  
  // "1s", "2s", "3s", "1p"... and "spast"  
  const out: NonNullable<VerbInflectedEntry\["inflection"\]> \= {  
    mood: "indicative",  
    voice: "active",  
    tense: "unknown",  
  };  
  
  for (const t of tags) {  
    const m \= /^(\[123\])(\[sp\])$/.exec(t);  
    if (m) {  
      out.person \= Number(m\[1\]) as 1 | 2 | 3;  
      out.number \= m\[2\] \=== "s" ? "singular" : "plural";  
      continue;  
    }  
    if (t \=== "spast") out.tense \= "simple\_past";  
    if (t \=== "pres") out.tense \= "present";  
  }  
  
  return out;  
}  
  
function decodeNominalInflTags(tags: string\[\]): { case\_: any; number?: any; gender?: any } {  
  // This is intentionally permissive: you will extend as you meet real tags.  
  let case\_: "nominative" | "genitive" | "accusative" | "vocative" | "unknown" \= "unknown";  
  let number: "singular" | "plural" | undefined;  
  let gender: "m" | "f" | "n" | "unknown" | undefined;  
  
  for (const t of tags) {  
    if (t \=== "nom") case\_ \= "nominative";  
    else if (t \=== "gen") case\_ \= "genitive";  
    else if (t \=== "acc") case\_ \= "accusative";  
    else if (t \=== "voc") case\_ \= "vocative";  
    else if (t \=== "s" || t \=== "sg") number \= "singular";  
    else if (t \=== "p" || t \=== "pl") number \= "plural";  
    else if (t \=== "m" || t \=== "f" || t \=== "n") gender \= t as any;  
  }  
  
  return { case\_, number, gender };  
}  
  
function normalizeGender(g: string): "m" | "f" | "n" | "unknown" {  
  if (g \=== "m" || g \=== "f" || g \=== "n") return g;  
  return "unknown";  
}  
  
function inferVerbEnding(form: string): string | undefined {  
  // minimal (you will extend)  
  if (form.endsWith("ω")) return "-ω";  
  if (form.endsWith("ομαι")) return "-ομαι";  
  if (form.endsWith("άω")) return "-άω";  
  if (form.endsWith("ώ")) return "-ώ";  
  return undefined;  
}  
  
function inferAugment(aorist: string | undefined): string | undefined {  
  if (!aorist) return undefined;  
  // Greek augment often appears as initial έ- / ή- etc.  
  if (aorist.startsWith("έ")) return "έ-";  
  if (aorist.startsWith("ή")) return "ή-";  
  return undefined;  
}  
  
function stripAugment(s: string | undefined): string | undefined {  
  if (!s) return undefined;  
  // extremely naive:  
  if (s.startsWith("έ")) return s.slice(1);  
  if (s.startsWith("ή")) return s.slice(1);  
  return s;  
}  
  
function ensureEndsWithE(stem: string): string {  
  // imperfect 3sg often ends with -ε; template gives "έγραφ"  
  return stem.endsWith("ε") ? stem : \`${stem}ε\`;  
}  
  
function inferPassiveAorist(elConj?: TemplateCall): string | undefined {  
  // For γράφω, p-simplepast looks like "γράφτ" which corresponds to "γράφτηκα".  
  const ps \= elConj?.named?.\["p-simplepast"\] ?? elConj?.named?.\["p-simplepast-2"\];  
  if (!ps) return undefined;  
  // heuristic: append "ηκα"  
  // (this is not universally correct, but gets your running example right)  
  return \`${ps}ηκα\`;  
}  
  
function extractDefinitionsFromWikitext(wt: string): string\[\] {  
  // Grab lines starting with "# " and strip some markup.  
  const lines \= wt.split(/\\r?\\n/);  
  const defs: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const line of lines) {  
    const m \= /^\\s\*#\\s+(.\*)\\s\*$/.exec(line);  
    if (!m) continue;  
    defs.push(stripWikitextInline(m\[1\]));  
  }  
  return defs;  
}  
  
function stripWikitextInline(s: string): string {  
  // very lightweight: remove links \[\[...\]\] and templates {{...}}.  
  // You’ll improve this later (or replace with a proper wikitext lib).  
  s \= s.replace(/\\{\\{\[^\]\*?\\}\\}/g, "");  
  s \= s.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^\\\]|\]+)\\|(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$2");  
  s \= s.replace(/\\\[\\\[(\[^\\\]\]+)\\\]\\\]/g, "$1");  
  s \= s.replace(/'''+/g, "");  
  s \= s.replace(/''+/g, "");  
  s \= s.replace(/\\s+/g, " ").trim();  
  return s;  
}  
  
function extractLinksFromRelatedTerms(wt: string, lang: "el"): string\[\] {  
  // Collect {{l|el|TERM|...}} calls anywhere in section (useful for Related terms).  
  const tpls \= extractTemplates(wt);  
  const links \= tpls  
    .filter(t => t.name \=== "l" && t.positional\[0\] \=== lang && typeof t.positional\[1\] \=== "string")  
    .map(t => t.positional\[1\])  
    .filter(Boolean);  
  
  // de-dupe preserving order  
  const seen \= new Set<string\>();  
  const out: string\[\] \= \[\];  
  for (const x of links) {  
    if (seen.has(x)) continue;  
    seen.add(x);  
    out.push(x);  
  }  
  return out;  
}
```

---

## 4) Why your earlier REST endpoint tests behaved like that

-   **Different Wiktionary language editions** do not always expose the same REST surface area consistently, and some endpoints reject cross-domain usage (“Domain not allowed”) depending on configuration.
    
-   The **MediaWiki Action API** (`w/api.php`) is the reliable baseline for Wikitext access across Wikimedia projects, and it explicitly supports parsing/sections/wikitext retrieval. [MediaWiki+1](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/API%3AParsing_wikitext?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    
-   Wiktionary itself is very explicit that it’s **not natively machine-readable** as a “data API”; you extract structure by parsing Wikitext/templates. [Wiktionary+1](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Wiktionary%3AParsing?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
    

---

## 1) Additions to your public API

```
TypeScript

export type WikiEnrichmentOptions \= {  
  /\*\* If true, attempt to attach Wikidata entity info (QID, sitelinks, image). \*/  
  includeWikidata?: boolean;  
  
  /\*\* Preferred languages for labels/description and Wikipedia sitelinks. \*/  
  wikidataLanguages?: string\[\]; // e.g. \["en","el","nl"\]  
  
  /\*\* If set, try to generate a thumbnail URL (px width). \*/  
  imageWidth?: number; // e.g. 320  
};  
  
export type Wiktionary SDKOptions \= {  
  lang?: "el";  
  posHint?: "verb" | "noun" | "adjective" | "participle" | "adverb" | "function" | "numeral";  
  edition?: "en";  
  followLemma?: boolean;  
  
  /\*\* New \*/  
  enrich?: WikiEnrichmentOptions;  
};  
  
export type WikidataEnrichment \= {  
  qid: string; // "Q…"  
  labels?: Record<string, string\>;  
  descriptions?: Record<string, string\>;  
  sitelinks?: Record<string, { site: string; title: string; url?: string }>;  
  images?: Array<{ filename: string; commonsUrl: string; thumbUrl?: string }>;  
};  
  
export type EnrichedEntry \= WiktionaryEntry & {  
  wikidata?: WikidataEnrichment;  
};
```

## 2) Robust homonymy + etymology-aware section model

On English Wiktionary, a Greek entry may look like:

-   `==Greek==` (level 2)
    
    -   `===Pronunciation===` (level 3)
        
    -   `===Etymology 1===` (level 3)
        
        -   `====Verb====` (level 4)
            
        -   `====Noun====` (level 4)
            
    -   `===Etymology 2===` (level 3)
        
        -   `====Noun====` (level 4)
            

So you need a small **section tree** rather than the simple “level-3 only” assumption.

### Fetch sections (Action API) and build a tree

```
TypeScript

type MWSection \= {  
  index: string;  
  line: string;  
  level: number; // numeric  
};  
  
type SectionNode \= MWSection & {  
  children: SectionNode\[\];  
};  
  
function buildSectionTree(sections: MWSection\[\]): SectionNode\[\] {  
  const root: SectionNode\[\] \= \[\];  
  const stack: SectionNode\[\] \= \[\];  
  
  for (const s of sections) {  
    const node: SectionNode \= { ...s, children: \[\] };  
  
    while (stack.length && stack\[stack.length \- 1\].level \>= node.level) stack.pop();  
    if (!stack.length) root.push(node);  
    else stack\[stack.length \- 1\].children.push(node);  
  
    stack.push(node);  
  }  
  
  return root;  
}  
  
function findLanguageNode(tree: SectionNode\[\], languageHeading: string): SectionNode | undefined {  
  return tree.find(n => n.level \=== 2 && n.line \=== languageHeading);  
}  
  
function isEtymologyHeading(line: string): boolean {  
  return /^Etymology\\s+\\d+$/i.test(line.trim());  
}  
  
function normalizePos(line: string): string {  
  return line.trim().toLowerCase();  
}
```

### Interpret Greek section into “blocks” (pronunciation + etymology blocks + PoS blocks)

```
TypeScript

type PosBlock \= { etymology?: string; pos: string; sectionIndex: string };  
type GreekLayout \= {  
  pronunciationSection?: string;  
  posBlocks: PosBlock\[\];  
};  
  
function extractGreekLayout(greekNode: SectionNode): GreekLayout {  
  const layout: GreekLayout \= { posBlocks: \[\] };  
  
  // Direct children of ==Greek== are typically level 3 headings:  
  // Pronunciation, Etymology 1/2, (or directly Verb/Noun/etc when no etymologies)  
  for (const child of greekNode.children) {  
    if (child.level !== 3) continue;  
  
    if (child.line \=== "Pronunciation") {  
      layout.pronunciationSection \= child.index;  
      continue;  
    }  
  
    if (isEtymologyHeading(child.line)) {  
      const et \= child.line;  
      // Under Etymology N we expect level 4 PoS sections  
      for (const posNode of child.children) {  
        if (posNode.level \=== 4) {  
          layout.posBlocks.push({ etymology: et, pos: normalizePos(posNode.line), sectionIndex: posNode.index });  
        }  
      }  
      continue;  
    }  
  
    // No etymology: PoS often appears at level 3 directly  
    layout.posBlocks.push({ pos: normalizePos(child.line), sectionIndex: child.index });  
  }  
  
  return layout;  
}
```

This is the key step for **homonymy**: you will return **multiple candidates**, each tagged with etymology if present.
